I received\r\nyour last letters--I am ashamed to confess: I lost several of them more\r\nthan a year ago, and did not answer you.... I will tell you presently\r\nwhy. But, evidently, you have always been dear to me: with the exception\r\nof yourself, there is no one of whom I wish to take leave, and perhaps I\r\nhave no one to whom I could bid farewell.\r\n\r\nSoon after my last letter to you (I was quite ready to set out for your\r\nparts, and was making various plans in advance), there happened to me an\r\nepisode which had, I may say, a strong influence on my fate,--so strong\r\nthat here I am, dying, thanks to that event. To wit: I set out for the\r\ntheatre, to see the ballet. I have never liked the ballet, and have\r\nalways felt a secret disgust for all sorts of actresses, singers, and\r\ndancers.... But, obviously, one cannot change his fate, neither does any\r\none know himself, and it is also impossible to foresee the future. In\r\npoint of fact, nothing happens in life except the unexpected, and we do\r\nnothing all our life long but adjust ourselves to events.... But I\r\nbelieve I am dropping into philosophy again. Old habit!... In a word, I\r\nfell in love with a dancer.\r\n\r\nThis was all the more strange because she could not be called a beauty.\r\nShe had, it is true, wonderful golden hair, with an ash tinge, and\r\nlarge, bright eyes, with a pensive and, at the same time, a bold\r\nglance.... Haven\xe2\x80\x99t I cause to know the expression of that glance? I\r\npined and languished for a whole year in its rays! She had a splendid\r\nfigure, and when she danced her folkdance, the spectators used to stamp\r\nand shout with rapture.... But I do not think any one besides myself\r\nfell in love with her--at all events, no one fell in love with her as I\r\ndid. From the very minute that I beheld her for the first time--(will\r\nyou believe it? all I have to do even now is to shut my eyes, and\r\nimmediately here stands before me the theatre, the almost empty stage,\r\nrepresenting the interior of a forest, and she runs out from behind the\r\nside-scenes on the right, with a wreath of vine-leaves on her head and a\r\ntiger-skin over her shoulders)--from that fatal minute I belonged to her\r\nwholly,--just as a dog belongs to his master; and if now, when I am\r\ndying, I do not belong to her, it is merely because she has cast me off.\r\n\r\nTo tell the truth, she never troubled herself especially about me. She\r\nbarely noticed me, although she good-naturedly made use of my money. I\r\nwas for her, as she expressed it in her broken French jargon, \xe2\x80\x9c_oun\r\nRousso buon enfan_,\xe2\x80\x9d--and nothing more. But I ... I could no longer live\r\nanywhere where she was not; I tore myself at one wrench from all that\r\nwas dear to me, from my native land itself, and set out in pursuit of\r\nthat woman.\r\n\r\nPerhaps you think that she was clever?--Not in the least! It sufficed to\r\ncast a glance at her low brow, it sufficed to note, if only once, her\r\nlazy, heedless smile, in order instantly to convince one\xe2\x80\x99s self as to\r\nthe paucity of her mental abilities. And I never imagined her to be a\r\nremarkable woman. On the whole, I did not deceive myself for a single\r\nminute on her score. But that did not help matters in the least.\r\nWhatever I thought of her in her absence, in her presence I felt nothing\r\nbut servile adoration.... In the German fairytales the knights often\r\nfall into that sort of stupor. I could not tear my eyes from her\r\nfeatures; I could not hear enough of her remarks, or sufficiently watch\r\nevery movement of hers; to tell the truth, I actually breathed to her\r\nbreathing. However, she was good-natured, unconstrained--too\r\nunconstrained even; she did not put on airs, as the majority of artists\r\ndo. She had a great deal of life, that is, a great deal of blood, of\r\nthat splendid Southern blood, into which the sun of their land must have\r\ndropped a portion of his rays. She slept nine hours a day, was fond of\r\ngood eating, never read a single line of print, unless, perhaps, the\r\narticles in the newspapers in which she was mentioned, and almost the\r\nsole tender sentiment in her life was her attachment to il signore\r\nCarlino, a small and greedy Italian who served as her secretary and whom\r\nshe afterward married. And with such a woman as this I, who have tasted\r\nso many varied intellectual subtleties, I, already an old man, could\r\nfall in love! Who could have expected it? I never expected it, at all\r\nevents. I did not anticipate the part which I should be compelled to\r\nplay. I did not expect that I should haunt rehearsals, freeze and get\r\nbored behind the scenes, inhale the reek of the theatre, make\r\nacquaintance with various unseemly individuals ... what am I\r\nsaying?--make acquaintance--bow to them. I had not expected that I\r\nshould carry a dancer\xe2\x80\x99s shawl, buy new gloves for her, clean her old\r\nones with white bread (but I did it, I take my oath!), cart home her\r\nbouquets, run about to the anterooms of journalists and directors, wear\r\nmyself out, give serenades, catch cold, lose my strength.... I had not\r\nexpected that I should acquire at last in a certain little German town\r\nthe ingenious nickname of \xe2\x80\x9c_der Kunst-barbar_.\xe2\x80\x9d... And all this in\r\nvain--in the fullest sense of the word, in vain! There, that is\r\nprecisely the state of the case....\r\n\r\nDo you remember how you and I, orally and by letter, argued about love,\r\ninto what subtleties we entered? And when it is put to the proof, it\r\nturns out that real love is a feeling not at all resembling that which\r\nwe imagined it to be. Love is not even a feeling at all; it is a malady,\r\na well-known condition of the soul and body. It does not develop\r\ngradually; there is no possibility of doubting it; one cannot dodge it,\r\nalthough it does not always manifest itself in identically the same\r\nfashion. It generally takes possession of a man without being invited,\r\nsuddenly, against his will--precisely like the cholera or a fever.... It\r\nlays hold upon him, the dear creature, as a hawk does upon a chicken;\r\nand it will bear him off whithersoever it wishes, struggle and resist as\r\nhe may.... In love there is no equality, no so-called free union of\r\nsouls and other ideal things, invented at their leisure by German\r\nprofessors.... No; in love one person is the slave, the other is the\r\nsovereign, and not without cause do the poets prate of the chains\r\nimposed by love. Yes, love is a chain, and the heaviest of chains at\r\nthat. At all events, I have arrived at that conviction, and have reached\r\nit by the path of experience. I have purchased that conviction at the\r\nprice of my life, because I am dying a slave.\r\n\r\nAlack, what a fate is mine! one thinks. In my youth I was resolutely\r\ndetermined to conquer heaven for myself.... Later on, I fell to dreaming\r\nabout the welfare of all mankind, the prosperity of my fatherland. Then\r\nthat passed off: I thought only of how I might arrange my domestic, my\r\nfamily life ... and I tripped over an ant-hill--and flop! I went\r\nheadlong on the ground, and into the grave.... What master hands we\r\nRussians are at winding up in that fashion!\r\n\r\nHowever, it is high time for me to turn away from all this,--it was time\r\nlong ago! May this burden fall from my soul along with my life! I wish\r\nfor the last time, if only for a moment, to enjoy that good, gentle\r\nfeeling which is diffused within me like a tranquil light as soon as I\r\ncall you to mind. Your image is now doubly dear to me.... Along with it\r\nthere surges up before me the image of my native land, and I waft to it\r\nand to you my last greeting. Live on, live long and happily, and\r\nremember one thing: whether you remain in that remote nook of the\r\nsteppes, where you sometimes find things so painful, but where I should\r\nso like to spend my last day, or whether you shall enter upon another\r\ncareer, remember: life fails to disappoint him alone who does not\r\nmeditate upon it, and, demanding nothing from it, calmly accepts its\r\nsparse gifts, and calmly makes use of them. Go forward, while you can:\r\nbut when your feet fail you,--sit down near the road, and gaze at the\r\npassers-by without vexation and without envy: for they will not go far!\r\nI have said this to you before, but death will teach any man whomsoever;\r\nmoreover, who shall say what is life, what is truth? Remember _who_ it\r\nwas that gave no answer to this question.... Farewell, M\xc3\xa1rya\r\nAlex\xc3\xa1ndrovna; farewell for the last time, and bear no ill will to poor--\r\n\r\nALEXY\xc3\x89I.\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\nTHE REGION OF DEAD CALM\r\n\r\n(1854)\r\n\r\n\r\nI\r\n\r\nIn a fairly-large recently-whitewashed chamber of a wing of the\r\nmanor-house in the village of S\xc3\xa1sovo, *** county, T*** Government, a\r\nyoung man in a paletot was sitting at a small, warped table, looking\r\nover accounts. Two stearine candles, in silver travelling-candlesticks,\r\nwere burning in front of him; in one corner, on the wall-bench, stood an\r\nopen bottle-case, in another a servant was setting up an iron bed. On\r\nthe other side of a low partition a samov\xc3\xa1r was murmuring and hissing; a\r\ndog was nestling about on some hay which had just been brought in. In\r\nthe doorway stood a peasant-man in a new overcoat girt with a red belt,\r\nwith a large beard, and an intelligent face--the overseer, judging by\r\nall the tokens. He was gazing attentively at the seated young man.\r\n\r\nAgainst one wall stood a very aged, tiny piano; beside it an\r\nequally-ancient chest of drawers with holes in place of the locks;\r\nbetween the windows a small, dim mirror was visible; on the\r\npartition-wall hung an old portrait, which was almost completely peeled\r\noff, representing a woman with powdered hair, in a _robe ronde_, and\r\nwith a black ribbon about her slender neck. Judging from the very\r\nperceptible sagging of the ceiling, and the slope of the floor, which\r\nwas full of cracks, the little wing into which we have conducted the\r\nreader had existed for a very long time. No one lived in it permanently;\r\nit was put to use when the owners came. The young man who was sitting at\r\nthe table was the owner of the village of S\xc3\xa1sovo. He had arrived only on\r\nthe previous day from his principal estate, situated a hundred\r\nversts[11] distant, and was preparing to depart on the morrow, after\r\ncompleting the inspection of the farming, listening to the demands of\r\nthe peasants, and verifying all the documents.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWell, that will do,\xe2\x80\x9d--he said, raising his head;--\xe2\x80\x9cI am tired. Thou\r\nmayest go now,\xe2\x80\x9d--he added, turning to the overseer;--\xe2\x80\x9cand come very\r\nearly to-morrow morning, and notify the peasants at daybreak that they\r\nare to present themselves in assembly,--dost hear me?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI obey.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd order the estate-clerk to present to me the report for the last\r\nmonth. But thou hast done well,\xe2\x80\x9d--the gentleman went on, casting a\r\nglance around him,--\xe2\x80\x9cin whitewashing the walls. Everything seems\r\ncleaner.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nThe overseer silently swept a glance around the walls also.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWell, go now.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nThe overseer made his obeisance and left the room.\r\n\r\nThe gentleman stretched himself.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHey!\xe2\x80\x9d--he shouted,--\xe2\x80\x9cGive me some tea!... \xe2\x80\x99Tis time to go to bed.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nHis servant went to the other side of the partition, and speedily\r\nreturned with a glass of tea, a bundle of town cracknels, and a\r\ncream-jug on an iron tray. The gentleman began to drink tea, but before\r\nhe had had time to swallow two mouthfuls, the noise of persons entering\r\nresounded from an adjoining room, and some one\xe2\x80\x99s squeaking voice\r\ninquired:\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIs Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch Ast\xc3\xa1khoff at home? Can he be seen?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nVlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch (that was the name of the young man in the paletot)\r\ncast a glance of surprise at his man, and said in a hurried whisper:\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cGo, find out who it is.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nThe man withdrew, slamming behind him the door, which closed badly.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnnounce to Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch,\xe2\x80\x9d--rang out the same squeaking voice as\r\nbefore,--\xe2\x80\x9cthat his neighbour Ip\xc3\xa1toff wishes to see him, if it will not\r\nincommode him; and another neighbour has come with me, Bodryak\xc3\xb3ff, Iv\xc3\xa1n\r\n\xc3\x8dlitch, who also desires to pay his respects.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nVlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch made an involuntary gesture of vexation.\r\nNevertheless, when his man entered the room, he said to him:\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAsk them in.\xe2\x80\x9d And he arose to receive his visitors.\r\n\r\nThe door opened, and the visitors made their appearance. One of them, a\r\nrobust, grey-haired little old man, with a small, round head and bright\r\nlittle eyes, walked in advance; the other, a tall, thin man of\r\nthree-and-thirty, with a long, swarthy face and dishevelled hair, walked\r\nbehind, with a shambling gait. The old man wore a neat grey coat with\r\nlarge, mother-of-pearl buttons; a small, pink neckerchief, half\r\nconcealed by the rolling collar of his white shirt, loosely encircled\r\nhis neck; his feet shone resplendent in gaiters; the plaids of his\r\nScotch trousers were agreeably gay in hue; and, altogether, he produced\r\na pleasant impression. His companion, on the contrary, evoked in the\r\nspectator a less favourable sensation: he wore an old black dress-coat,\r\nbuttoned up to the throat; his full trousers, of thick, winter tricot,\r\nmatched his coat in colour; no linen was visible, either around his\r\nthroat or around his wrists. The little old man was the first to\r\napproach Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch, and, with an amiable inclination of the\r\nhead, he began in the same shrill little voice:\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI have the honour to introduce myself,--your nearest neighbour, and\r\neven a relative, Ip\xc3\xa1toff, Mikha\xc3\xadlo Nikol\xc3\xa1itch. I have long wished to\r\nhave the pleasure of making your acquaintance. I hope that I have not\r\ndisturbed you.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nVlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch replied that he was very glad to see him, and that\r\nhe was not disturbed in the least, and would not he take a seat ... and\r\ndrink tea.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd this nobleman,\xe2\x80\x9d--went on the little old man, after listening with a\r\ncourteous smile to Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch\xe2\x80\x99s unfinished phrases, and\r\nextending his hand in the direction of the gentleman in the\r\ndress-coat,--\xe2\x80\x9calso your neighbour ... and my good acquaintance, Iv\xc3\xa1n\r\n\xc3\x8dlitch, strongly desired to make your acquaintance.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nThe gentleman in the dress-coat, from whose countenance no one would\r\nhave suspected that he was capable of desiring anything strongly in his\r\nlife--so preoccupied and, at the same time, so sleepy was the expression\r\nof that countenance,--the gentleman in the dress-coat bowed clumsily and\r\nlanguidly. Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch bowed to him in return, and again invited\r\nthe visitors to be seated.\r\n\r\nThe visitors sat down.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI am very glad,\xe2\x80\x9d--began the little old man, pleasantly throwing apart\r\nhis hands, while his companion set to scrutinising the ceiling, with his\r\nmouth slightly open:--\xe2\x80\x9cI am very glad that I have, at last, the honour\r\nof seeing you personally. Although you have your permanent residence in\r\na county which lies at a considerable distance from these localities,\r\nstill, we regard you also as one of our own primordial landed\r\nproprietors, so to speak.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThat is very flattering to me,\xe2\x80\x9d--returned Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cFlattering or not, it is a fact. You must excuse us, Vlad\xc3\xadmir\r\nSergy\xc3\xa9itch; we people here in *** county are a straightforward folk; we\r\nlive in our simplicity; we say what we think, without circumlocution. It\r\nis our custom, I must tell you, not to call upon each other on\r\nName-days[12] otherwise than in our frock-coats. Truly! We have made\r\nthat the rule. On that account, we are called \xe2\x80\x98frock-coaters\xe2\x80\x99 in the\r\nadjoining counties, and we are even reproached for our bad style; but we\r\npay no attention to that! Pray, what is the use of living in the\r\ncountry--and then standing on ceremony?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOf course, what can be better ... in the country ... than that\r\nnaturalness of intercourse,\xe2\x80\x9d--remarked Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd yet,\xe2\x80\x9d--replied the little old man,--\xe2\x80\x9camong us in our county dwell\r\npeople of the cleverest sort,--one may say people of European culture,\r\nalthough they do not wear dress-suits. Take, for example, our historian\r\nEvsiuk\xc3\xb3ff, Step\xc3\xa1n Step\xc3\xa1nitch: he is interesting himself in Russian\r\nhistory from the most ancient times, and is known in Petersburg--an\r\nextremely learned man! There is in our town an ancient Swedish\r\ncannon-ball ... \xe2\x80\x99tis placed yonder, in the centre of the public square\r\n... and \xe2\x80\x99twas he who discovered it, you know! Certainly! Tz\xc3\xa9nteler,\r\nAnt\xc3\xb3n K\xc3\xa1rlitch ... now he has studied natural history; but they say all\r\nGermans are successful in that line. When, ten years ago, a stray hyena\r\nwas killed in our vicinity, it was this Ant\xc3\xb3n K\xc3\xa1rlitch who discovered\r\nthat it really was a hyena, by cause of the peculiar construction of its\r\ntail. And then, we have a landed proprietor Kaburd\xc3\xadn: he chiefly writes\r\nlight articles; he wields a very dashing pen; his articles appear in\r\n\xe2\x80\x98Galatea.\xe2\x80\x99 Bodryak\xc3\xb3ff, ... not Iv\xc3\xa1n \xc3\x8dlitch; no, Iv\xc3\xa1n \xc3\x8dlitch neglects\r\nthat; but another Bodryak\xc3\xb3ff, Sergy\xc3\xa9i ... what the deuce was his\r\nfather\xe2\x80\x99s baptismal name, Iv\xc3\xa1n \xc3\x8dlitch ... what the deuce was it?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cSergy\xc3\xa9itch,\xe2\x80\x9d--prompted Iv\xc3\xa1n \xc3\x8dlitch.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes; Sergy\xc3\xa9i Sergy\xc3\xa9itch,--he busies himself with writing verses. Well,\r\nof course he\xe2\x80\x99s not a P\xc3\xbashkin, but sometimes he gets off things which\r\nwould pass muster even in the capitals. Do you know his epigram on Ag\xc3\xa9i\r\nF\xc3\xb3mitch?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat Ag\xc3\xa9i F\xc3\xb3mitch?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAkh, pardon me; I keep forgetting that you are not a resident here,\r\nafter all. He is our chief of police. The epigram is extremely amusing.\r\nThou rememberest it, I believe, Iv\xc3\xa1n \xc3\x8dlitch?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAg\xc3\xa9i F\xc3\xb3mitch,\xe2\x80\x9d--said Bodryak\xc3\xb3ff, indifferently--\r\n\r\n    \xe2\x80\x9c ... not without cause is gloriously\r\n     By the nobles\xe2\x80\x99 election honoured....\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI must tell you,\xe2\x80\x9d--broke in Ip\xc3\xa1toff,--\xe2\x80\x9cthat he was elected almost\r\nexclusively by white balls, for he is a most worthy man.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAg\xc3\xa9i F\xc3\xb3mitch,\xe2\x80\x9d--repeated Bodryak\xc3\xb3ff,\r\n\r\n    \xe2\x80\x9c ... not without cause is gloriously\r\n     By the nobles\xe2\x80\x99 election honoured:\r\n     He drinks and eats regularly....\r\n     So why should not he be the regulator of order?\xe2\x80\x9d[13]\r\n\r\nThe little old man burst out laughing.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHa, ha, ha! that isn\xe2\x80\x99t bad, is it? Ever since then, if you\xe2\x80\x99ll believe\r\nme, each one of us will say, for instance, to Ag\xc3\xa9i F\xc3\xb3mitch: \xe2\x80\x98Good\r\nmorning!\xe2\x80\x99--and will invariably add: \xe2\x80\x98so why should not he be the\r\nregulator of order?\xe2\x80\x99 And does Ag\xc3\xa9i F\xc3\xb3mitch get angry, think you? Not in\r\nthe least. No--that\xe2\x80\x99s not our way. Just ask Iv\xc3\xa1n \xc3\x8dlitch here if it is.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nIv\xc3\xa1n \xc3\x8dlitch merely rolled up his eyes.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cGet angry at a jest--how is that possible? Now, take Iv\xc3\xa1n \xc3\x8dlitch\r\nthere; his nickname among us is \xe2\x80\x98The Folding Soul,\xe2\x80\x99 because he agrees to\r\neverything very promptly. What then? Does Iv\xc3\xa1n \xc3\x8dlitch take offence at\r\nthat? Never!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nIv\xc3\xa1n \xc3\x8dlitch, slowly blinking his eyes, looked first at the little old\r\nman, then at Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch.\r\n\r\nThe epithet, \xe2\x80\x9cThe Folding Soul,\xe2\x80\x9d really did fit Iv\xc3\xa1n \xc3\x8dlitch admirably.\r\nThere was not a trace in him of what is called will or character. Any\r\none who wished could lead him whithersoever he would; all that was\r\nnecessary was to say to him: \xe2\x80\x9cCome on, Iv\xc3\xa1n \xc3\x8dlitch!\xe2\x80\x9d--and he picked up\r\nhis cap and went; but if another person turned up, and said to him:\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHalt, Iv\xc3\xa1n \xc3\x8dlitch!\xe2\x80\x9d--he laid down his cap and remained. He was of a\r\npeaceable, tranquil disposition, had lived a bachelor-life, did not play\r\ncards, but was fond of sitting beside the players and looking into each\r\nof their faces in turn. Without society he could not exist, and solitude\r\nhe could not endure. At such times he became despondent; however, this\r\nhappened very rarely with him. He had another peculiarity: rising from\r\nhis bed betimes in the morning, he would sing in an undertone an old\r\nromance:\r\n\r\n    \xe2\x80\x9cIn the country once a Baron\r\n     Dwelt in simplicity rural....\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nIn consequence of this peculiarity of Iv\xc3\xa1n \xc3\x8dlitch\xe2\x80\x99s, he was also called\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThe Hawfinch,\xe2\x80\x9d because, as is well known, the hawfinch when in\r\ncaptivity sings only once in the course of the day, early in the\r\nmorning. Such was Iv\xc3\xa1n \xc3\x8dlitch Bodryak\xc3\xb3ff.\r\n\r\nThe conversation between Ip\xc3\xa1toff and Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch lasted for\r\nquite a long time, but not in its original, so to speak, speculative\r\ndirection. The little old man questioned Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch about his\r\nestate, the condition of his forests and other sorts of land, the\r\nimprovements which he had already introduced or was only intending to\r\nintroduce in his farming; he imparted to him several of his own\r\nobservations; advised him, among other things, in order to get rid of\r\nhummocky pastures, to sprinkle them with oats, which, he said, would\r\ninduce the pigs to plough them up with their snouts, and so forth. But,\r\nat last, perceiving that Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch was so sleepy that he could\r\nhardly keep his eyes open, and that a certain deliberation and\r\nincoherence were making themselves evident in his speech, the little old\r\nman rose, and, with a courteous obeisance, declared that he would not\r\nincommode him any longer with his presence, but that he hoped to have\r\nthe pleasure of seeing the valued guest at his own house not later than\r\nthe following day, at dinner.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd the first person you meet, not to mention any small child, but, so\r\nto speak, any hen or peasant-woman,\xe2\x80\x9d--he added,--\xe2\x80\x9cwill point out to you\r\nthe road to my village. All you have to do is to ask for Ip\xc3\xa1toff. The\r\nhorses will trot there of themselves.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nVlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch replied with a little hesitation--which, however,\r\nwas natural to him--that he would try ... that if nothing prevented....\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes, we shall certainly expect you,\xe2\x80\x9d--the little old man interrupted\r\nhim, cordially, shook his hand warmly, and briskly withdrew, exclaiming\r\nin the doorway, as he half turned round:--\xe2\x80\x9cWithout ceremony!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cFolding Soul\xe2\x80\x9d Bodryak\xc3\xb3ff bowed in silence and vanished in the wake of\r\nhis companion, with a preliminary stumble on the threshold.\r\n\r\nHaving seen his unexpected guests off, Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch immediately\r\nundressed, got into bed, and went to sleep.\r\n\r\nVlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch Ast\xc3\xa1khoff belonged to the category of people who,\r\nafter having cautiously tested their powers in two or three different\r\ncareers, are wont to say of themselves that they have finally come to\r\nthe conclusion to look at life from a practical point of view, and who\r\ndevote their leisure to augmenting their revenues. He was not stupid,\r\nwas rather penurious, and very sensible; was fond of reading, of\r\nsociety, of music--but all in moderation ... and bore himself very\r\ndecorously. He was twenty-seven years old. A great many young men of\r\nhis sort have sprung up recently. He was of medium height, well built,\r\nand had agreeable though small features; their expression almost never\r\nvaried; his eyes always gleamed with one and the same stern, bright\r\nglance; only now and then did this glance soften with a faint shade of\r\nsomething which was not precisely sadness, nor yet precisely boredom; a\r\ncourteous smile rarely quitted his lips. He had very handsome, fair\r\nhair, silky, and falling in long ringlets. Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch owned\r\nabout six hundred souls[14] on a good estate, and he was thinking of\r\nmarriage--a marriage of inclination, but which should, at the same time,\r\nbe advantageous. He was particularly desirous of finding a wife with\r\npowerful connections. In a word, he merited the appellation of\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cgentleman\xe2\x80\x9d which had recently come into vogue.\r\n\r\nWhen he rose on the following morning, very early, according to his\r\nwont, our gentleman occupied himself with business, and, we must do him\r\nthe justice to say, did so in a decidedly practical manner, which cannot\r\nalways be said of practical young men among us in Russia. He patiently\r\nlistened to the confused petitions and complaints of the peasants, gave\r\nthem satisfaction so far as he was able, investigated the quarrels and\r\ndissensions which had arisen between relatives, exhorted some, scolded\r\nothers, audited the clerk\xe2\x80\x99s accounts, brought to light two or three\r\nrascalities on the part of the overseer--in a word, handled matters in\r\nsuch wise that he was very well satisfied with himself, and the\r\npeasants, as they returned from the assembly to their homes, spoke well\r\nof him.\r\n\r\nIn spite of his promise given on the preceding evening to Ip\xc3\xa1toff,\r\nVlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch had made up his mind to dine at home, and had even\r\nordered his travelling-cook to prepare his favourite rice-soup with\r\npluck; but all of a sudden, possibly in consequence of that feeling of\r\nsatisfaction which had filled his soul ever since the early morning, he\r\nstopped short in the middle of the room, smote himself on the brow with\r\nhis hand, and, not without some spirit, exclaimed aloud: \xe2\x80\x9cI believe I\xe2\x80\x99ll\r\ngo to that flowery old babbler!\xe2\x80\x9d No sooner said than done; half an hour\r\nlater he was sitting in his new tarant\xc3\xa1s, drawn by four stout\r\npeasant-horses, and driving to Ip\xc3\xa1toff\xe2\x80\x99s house, which was reckoned to be\r\nnot more than twenty-five versts distant by a capital road.\r\n\r\n\r\nII\r\n\r\nMikha\xc3\xadlo Nikol\xc3\xa1evitch Ip\xc3\xa1toff\xe2\x80\x99s manor consisted of two separate small\r\nmansions, built opposite each other on the two sides of a huge pond\r\nthrough which ran a river. A long dam, planted with silver poplars,\r\nshut off the pond; almost on a level with it the red roof of a small\r\nhand-mill was visible. Built exactly alike, and painted with the same\r\nlilac hue, the tiny houses seemed to be exchanging glances across the\r\nbroad, watery expanse, with the glittering panes of their small, clean\r\nwindows. From the middle of each little house a circular terrace\r\nprojected, and a sharp-peaked pediment rose aloft, supported by four\r\nwhite pillars set close together. The ancient park ran all the way round\r\nthe pond; lindens stretched out in alleys, and stood in dense clumps;\r\naged pine-trees, with pale yellow boles, dark oaks, magnificent maples\r\nhere and there reared high in air their solitary crests; the dense\r\nverdure of the thickly-spreading lilacs and acacias advanced close up to\r\nthe very sides of the two little houses, leaving revealed only their\r\nfronts, from which winding paths paved with brick ran down the slope.\r\nMotley-hued ducks, white and grey geese were swimming in separate flocks\r\non the clear water of the pond; it never became covered with scum,\r\nthanks to abundant springs which welled into its \xe2\x80\x9chead\xe2\x80\x9d from the base of\r\nthe steep, rocky ravine. The situation of the manor was good, pleasant,\r\nisolated, and beautiful.\r\n\r\nIn one of the two little houses dwelt Mikha\xc3\xadl Nikol\xc3\xa1evitch himself; in\r\nthe other lived his mother, a decrepit old woman of seventy years. When\r\nhe drove on to the dam, Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch did not know to which house\r\nto betake himself. He glanced about him: a small urchin of the\r\nhouse-serfs was fishing, as he stood barefooted on a half-rotten\r\ntree-stump. Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch hailed him.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBut to whom are you going--to the old lady or to the young\r\nmaster?\xe2\x80\x9d--replied the urchin, without taking his eyes from his float.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat lady?\xe2\x80\x9d--replied Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch.--\xe2\x80\x9cI want to find Mikha\xc3\xadlo\r\nNikol\xc3\xa1itch.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAh! the young master? Well, then, turn to the right.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nAnd the lad gave his line a jerk, and drew from the motionless water a\r\nsmall, silvery carp. Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch drove to the right.\r\n\r\nMikha\xc3\xadl Nikol\xc3\xa1itch was playing at draughts with The Folding Soul when\r\nthe arrival of Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch was announced to him. He was\r\ndelighted, sprang from his arm-chair, ran out into the anteroom and\r\nthere kissed the visitor three times.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou find me with my invariable friend, Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch,\xe2\x80\x9d--began the\r\nloquacious little old man:--\xe2\x80\x9cwith Iv\xc3\xa1n \xc3\x8dlitch, who, I will remark in\r\npassing, is completely enchanted with your affability.\xe2\x80\x9d (Iv\xc3\xa1n \xc3\x8dlitch\r\ndarted a silent glance at the corner.) \xe2\x80\x9cHe was so kind as to remain to\r\nplay draughts with me, while all my household went for a stroll in the\r\npark; but I will send for them at once....\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBut why disturb them?\xe2\x80\x9d--Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch tried to expostulate....\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNot the least inconvenience, I assure you. Hey, there, V\xc3\xa1nka, run for\r\nthe young ladies as fast as thou canst ... tell them that a guest has\r\nfavoured us with a visit. And how does this locality please you? It\xe2\x80\x99s\r\nnot bad, is it? Kaburd\xc3\xadn has composed some verses about it. \xe2\x80\x98Ip\xc3\xa1tovka,\r\nrefuge lovely\xe2\x80\x99--that\xe2\x80\x99s the way they begin,--and the rest of it is just\r\nas good, only I don\xe2\x80\x99t remember all of it. The park is large, that\xe2\x80\x99s the\r\ntrouble; beyond my means. And these two houses, which are so much alike,\r\nas you have, perhaps, deigned to observe, were erected by two\r\nbrothers--my father Nikol\xc3\xa1i, and my uncle Sergy\xc3\xa9i; they also laid out\r\nthe park; they were exemplary friends ... Damon and ... there now! I\xe2\x80\x99ve\r\nforgotten the other man\xe2\x80\x99s name....\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cPythion,\xe2\x80\x9d--remarked Iv\xc3\xa1n \xc3\x8dlitch.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNot really? Well, never mind.\xe2\x80\x9d (At home the old man talked in a much\r\nmore unconventional manner than when he was paying calls.)--\xe2\x80\x9cYou are,\r\nprobably, not ignorant of the fact, Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch, that I am a\r\nwidower, that I have lost my wife; my elder children are in government\r\neducational institutions,[15] and I have with me only the youngest two,\r\nand my sister-in-law lives with me--my wife\xe2\x80\x99s sister; you will see her\r\ndirectly. But why don\xe2\x80\x99t I offer you some refreshment? Iv\xc3\xa1n \xc3\x8dlitch, my\r\ndear fellow, see to a little luncheon ... what sort of vodka are you\r\npleased to prefer?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI drink nothing until dinner.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cGoodness, how is that possible! However, as you please. The truest\r\nhospitality is to let the guest do as he likes. We are very\r\nsimple-mannered folk here, you see. Here with us, if I may venture so to\r\nexpress myself, we live not so much in a lonely as in a dead-calm place,\r\na remote nook--that\xe2\x80\x99s what! But why don\xe2\x80\x99t you sit down?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nVlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch seated himself, without letting go of his hat.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cPermit me to relieve you,\xe2\x80\x9d--said Ip\xc3\xa1toff, and delicately taking his hat\r\nfrom him, he carried it off to a corner, then returned, looked his\r\nvisitor in the eye with a cordial smile, and, not knowing just what\r\nagreeable thing to say to him, inquired, in the most hearty\r\nmanner,--whether he was fond of playing draughts.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI play all games badly,\xe2\x80\x9d--replied Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd that\xe2\x80\x99s a very fine thing in you,\xe2\x80\x9d--returned Ip\xc3\xa1toff:--\xe2\x80\x9cbut draughts\r\nis not a game, but rather a diversion--a way of passing leisure time;\r\nisn\xe2\x80\x99t that so, Iv\xc3\xa1n \xc3\x8dlitch?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nIv\xc3\xa1n \xc3\x8dlitch cast an indifferent glance at Ip\xc3\xa1toff, as though he were\r\nthinking to himself, \xe2\x80\x9cThe devil only knows whether it is a game or a\r\ndiversion,\xe2\x80\x9d but, after waiting a while, he said:\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes; draughts don\xe2\x80\x99t count.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cChess is quite another matter, they say,\xe2\x80\x9d--pursued Ip\xc3\xa1toff;--\xe2\x80\x9c\xe2\x80\x99tis a\r\nvery difficult game, I\xe2\x80\x99m told. But, in my opinion ... but yonder come my\r\npeople!\xe2\x80\x9d--he interrupted himself, glancing through the half-open glass\r\ndoor, which gave upon the park.\r\n\r\nVlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch rose, turned round, and beheld first two little\r\ngirls, about ten years of age, in pink cotton frocks and broad-brimmed\r\nhats, who were running alertly up the steps of the terrace; not far\r\nbehind them a tall, plump, well-built young girl of twenty, in a dark\r\ngown, made her appearance. They all entered the house, and the little\r\ngirls courtesied sedately to the visitor.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHere, sir, let me present you,\xe2\x80\x9d--said the host;--\xe2\x80\x9cmy daughters, sir.\r\nThis one here is named K\xc3\xa1tya, and this one is N\xc3\xa1stya, and this is my\r\nsister-in-law, M\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna, whom I have already had the pleasure of\r\nmentioning to you. I beg that you will love and favour them.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nVlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch made his bow to M\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna; she replied to him\r\nwith a barely perceptible inclination of the head.\r\n\r\nM\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna held in her hand a large, open knife; her thick,\r\nruddy-blond hair was slightly dishevelled,--a small green leaf had got\r\nentangled in it, her braids had escaped from the comb,--her\r\ndark-skinned face was flushed, and her red lips were parted; her gown\r\nlooked crumpled. She was breathing fast; her eyes were sparkling; it was\r\nevident that she had been working in the garden. She immediately left\r\nthe room; the little girls ran out after her.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cShe\xe2\x80\x99s going to rearrange her toilet a bit,\xe2\x80\x9d--remarked the old man,\r\nturning to Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch;--\xe2\x80\x9cthey can\xe2\x80\x99t get along without that,\r\nsir!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nVlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch grinned at him in response, and became somewhat\r\npensive. M\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna had made an impression on him. It was long since\r\nhe had seen such a purely Russian beauty of the steppes. She speedily\r\nreturned, sat down on the divan, and remained motionless. She had\r\nsmoothed her hair, but had not changed her gown,--had not even put on\r\ncuffs. Her features expressed not precisely pride, but rather austerity,\r\nalmost harshness; her brow was broad and low, her nose short and\r\nstraight; a slow, lazy smile curled her lips from time to time; her\r\nstraight eyebrows contracted scornfully. She kept her large, dark eyes\r\nalmost constantly lowered. \xe2\x80\x9cI know,\xe2\x80\x9d her repellent young face seemed to\r\nbe saying; \xe2\x80\x9cI know that you are all looking at me; well, then, look; you\r\nbore me.\xe2\x80\x9d But when she raised her eyes, there was something wild,\r\nbeautiful, and stolid about them, which was suggestive of the eyes of a\r\ndoe. She had a magnificent figure. A classical poet would have compared\r\nher to Ceres or Juno.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat have you been doing in the garden?\xe2\x80\x9d--Ip\xc3\xa1toff asked her, being\r\ndesirous of bringing her into the conversation.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI have been cutting off dead branches, and digging up the flower-beds,\xe2\x80\x9d\r\nshe replied, in a voice which was rather low, but agreeable and\r\nresonant.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd are you tired?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThe children are; I am not.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI know,\xe2\x80\x9d--interposed the old man, with a smile;--\xe2\x80\x9cthou art a regular\r\nBob\xc3\xa9lina! And have you been to grandmamma\xe2\x80\x99s?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes; she is asleep.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAre you fond of flowers?\xe2\x80\x9d--Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch asked her.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhy dost thou not put on thy hat when thou goest out of\r\ndoors?\xe2\x80\x9d--Ip\xc3\xa1toff remarked to her.--\xe2\x80\x9cJust see how red and sunburned thou\r\nart.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nShe silently passed her hand over her face. Her hands were not large,\r\nbut rather broad, and decidedly red. She did not wear gloves.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd are you fond of gardening?\xe2\x80\x9d--Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch put another\r\nquestion to her.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nVlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch began to narrate what a fine garden there was in his\r\nneighbourhood, belonging to a wealthy landed proprietor named\r\nN***.--The head gardener, a German, received in wages alone two thousand\r\nrubles, silver[16]--he said, among other things.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd what is the name of that gardener?\xe2\x80\x9d--inquired Iv\xc3\xa1n \xc3\x8dlitch,\r\nsuddenly.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI don\xe2\x80\x99t remember,--Meyer or M\xc3\xbcller, I think. But why do you ask?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cFor no reason in particular, sir,\xe2\x80\x9d--replied Iv\xc3\xa1n \xc3\x8dlitch.--\xe2\x80\x9cTo find out\r\nhis name.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nVlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch continued his narration. The little girls, Mikha\xc3\xadl\r\nNikol\xc3\xa1itch\xe2\x80\x99s daughters, entered, sat down quietly, and quietly began to\r\nlisten....\r\n\r\nA servant made his appearance at the door, had announced that Eg\xc3\xb3r\r\nKap\xc3\xadtonitch had arrived.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAh! Ask him in, ask him in!\xe2\x80\x9d--exclaimed Ip\xc3\xa1toff.\r\n\r\nThere entered a short, fat little old man, one of the sort of people who\r\nare called squat or dumpy, with a puffy and, at the same time, a\r\nwrinkled little face, after the fashion of a baked apple. He wore a grey\r\nhussar jacket with black braiding and a standing collar; his full\r\ncoffee-coloured velveteen trousers ended far above his ankles.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cGood morning, my most respected Eg\xc3\xb3r Kap\xc3\xadtonitch,\xe2\x80\x9d--exclaimed Ip\xc3\xa1toff,\r\nadvancing to meet him.--\xe2\x80\x9cWe haven\xe2\x80\x99t seen each other for a long time.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cCouldn\xe2\x80\x99t be helped,\xe2\x80\x9d--returned Eg\xc3\xb3r Kap\xc3\xadtonitch in a lisping and\r\nwhining voice, after having preliminarily exchanged salutations with all\r\npresent;--\xe2\x80\x9csurely you know, Mikha\xc3\xadl Sergy\xc3\xa9itch, whether I am a free man\r\nor not?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd how are you not a free man, Eg\xc3\xb3r Kap\xc3\xadtonitch?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhy, of course I\xe2\x80\x99m not, Mikha\xc3\xadl Nikol\xc3\xa1itch; there\xe2\x80\x99s my family, my\r\naffairs.... And there\xe2\x80\x99s Matry\xc3\xb3na M\xc3\xa1rkovna to boot,\xe2\x80\x9d and he waved his\r\nhand in despair.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBut what about Matry\xc3\xb3na M\xc3\xa1rkovna?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nAnd Ip\xc3\xa1toff launched a slight wink at Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch, as though\r\ndesirous of exciting his interest in advance.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhy, everybody knows,\xe2\x80\x9d--returned Eg\xc3\xb3r Kap\xc3\xadtonitch, as he took a\r\nseat;--\xe2\x80\x9cshe\xe2\x80\x99s always discontented with me, don\xe2\x80\x99t you know that? Whatever\r\nI say, it\xe2\x80\x99s wrong, not delicate, not decorous. And why it isn\xe2\x80\x99t\r\ndecorous, the Lord God alone knows. And the young ladies, my daughters\r\nthat is to say, do the same, taking pattern by their mother. I don\xe2\x80\x99t say\r\nbut what Matry\xc3\xb3na M\xc3\xa1rkovna is a very fine woman, but she\xe2\x80\x99s awfully\r\nsevere on the score of manners.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBut, good gracious! in what way are your manners bad, Eg\xc3\xb3r\r\nKap\xc3\xadtonitch?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThat\xe2\x80\x99s exactly what I\xe2\x80\x99d like to know myself; but, evidently, she\xe2\x80\x99s\r\nhard to suit. Yesterday, for instance, I said at table: \xe2\x80\x98Matry\xc3\xb3na\r\nM\xc3\xa1rkovna,\xe2\x80\x99\xe2\x80\x9d and Eg\xc3\xb3r Kap\xc3\xadtonitch imparted to his voice an insinuating\r\ninflection,--\xe2\x80\x9c\xe2\x80\x98Matry\xc3\xb3na M\xc3\xa1rkovna,\xe2\x80\x99 says I, \xe2\x80\x98what\xe2\x80\x99s the meaning of\r\nthis,--that Ald\xc3\xb3shka isn\xe2\x80\x99t careful with the horses, doesn\xe2\x80\x99t know how to\r\ndrive?\xe2\x80\x99 says I; \xe2\x80\x98there\xe2\x80\x99s the black stallion quite foundered.\xe2\x80\x99--I-iikh!\r\nhow Matry\xc3\xb3na M\xc3\xa1rkovna did flare up, and set to crying shame on me: \xe2\x80\x98Thou\r\ndost not know how to express thyself decently in the society of ladies,\xe2\x80\x99\r\nsays she; and the young ladies instantly galloped away from the table,\r\nand on the next day, the Biri\xc3\xbaloff young ladies, my wife\xe2\x80\x99s nieces, had\r\nheard all about it. And how had I expressed myself badly? And no matter\r\nwhat I say--and sometimes I really am incautious,--no matter to whom I\r\nsay it, especially at home,--those Biri\xc3\xbaloff girls know all about it the\r\nnext day. A fellow simply doesn\xe2\x80\x99t know what to do. Sometimes I\xe2\x80\x99m just\r\nsitting so, thinking after my fashion,--I breathe hard, as perhaps you\r\nknow,--and Matry\xc3\xb3na M\xc3\xa1rkovna sets to berating me again: \xe2\x80\x98Don\xe2\x80\x99t snore,\xe2\x80\x99\r\nsays she; \xe2\x80\x98nobody snores nowadays!\xe2\x80\x99--\xe2\x80\x98What art thou scolding about,\r\nMatry\xc3\xb3na M\xc3\xa1rkovna?\xe2\x80\x99 says I. \xe2\x80\x98Good mercy, thou shouldst have compassion,\r\nbut thou scoldest.\xe2\x80\x99 So I don\xe2\x80\x99t meditate at home any more. I sit and look\r\ndown--so--all the time. By Heaven, I do. And then, again, not long ago,\r\nwe got into bed; \xe2\x80\x98Matry\xc3\xb3na M\xc3\xa1rkovna,\xe2\x80\x99 says I, \xe2\x80\x98what makes thee spoil\r\nthy page-boy, m\xc3\xa1tushka?[17] Why, he\xe2\x80\x99s a regular little pig,\xe2\x80\x99 says I,\r\n\xe2\x80\x98and he might wash his face of a Sunday, at least.\xe2\x80\x99 And what happened?\r\nIt strikes me that I said it distantly, tenderly, but I didn\xe2\x80\x99t hit the\r\nmark even then; Matry\xc3\xb3na M\xc3\xa1rkovna began to cry shame on me again: \xe2\x80\x98Thou\r\ndost not understand how to behave in the society of ladies,\xe2\x80\x99 says she;\r\nand the next day the Biri\xc3\xbaloff girls knew all about it. What time have I\r\nto think of visits under such circumstances, Mikha\xc3\xadl Nikol\xc3\xa1itch?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99m amazed at what you tell me,\xe2\x80\x9d--replied Ip\xc3\xa1toff;--\xe2\x80\x9cI did not expect\r\nthat from Matry\xc3\xb3na M\xc3\xa1rkovna. Apparently, she is....\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAn extremely fine woman,\xe2\x80\x9d--put in Eg\xc3\xb3r Kap\xc3\xadtonitch;--\xe2\x80\x9ca model wife and\r\nmother, so to speak, only strict on the score of manners. She says that\r\n_ensemble_ is necessary in everything, and that I haven\xe2\x80\x99t got it. I\r\ndon\xe2\x80\x99t speak French, as you are aware, I only understand it. But what\xe2\x80\x99s\r\nthat _ensemble_ that I haven\xe2\x80\x99t got?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nIp\xc3\xa1toff, who was not very strong in French himself, only shrugged his\r\nshoulders.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd how are your children--your sons, that is to say?\xe2\x80\x9d--he asked Eg\xc3\xb3r\r\nKap\xc3\xadtonitch after a brief pause.\r\n\r\nEg\xc3\xb3r Kap\xc3\xadtonitch darted an oblique glance at him.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cMy sons are all right. I\xe2\x80\x99m satisfied with them. The girls have got out\r\nof hand, but I\xe2\x80\x99m satisfied with my sons. Ly\xc3\xb3lya discharges his service\r\nwell, his superior officers approve of him; that Ly\xc3\xb3lya of mine is a\r\nclever fellow. Well, M\xc3\xadkhetz--he\xe2\x80\x99s not like that; he has turned out some\r\nsort of a philanthropist.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhy a philanthropist?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThe Lord knows; he speaks to nobody, he shuns folks. Matry\xc3\xb3na M\xc3\xa1rkovna\r\nmostly abashes him. \xe2\x80\x98Why dost thou take pattern by thy father?\xe2\x80\x99 she says\r\nto him. \xe2\x80\x98Do thou respect him, but copy thy mother as to manners.\xe2\x80\x99 He\xe2\x80\x99ll\r\nget straightened out, he\xe2\x80\x99ll turn out all right also.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nVlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch asked Ip\xc3\xa1toff to introduce him to Eg\xc3\xb3r Kap\xc3\xadtonitch.\r\nThey entered into conversation. M\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna did not take part in it;\r\nIv\xc3\xa1n \xc3\x8dlitch seated himself beside her, and said two words, in all, to\r\nher; the little girls came up to him, and began to narrate something to\r\nhim in a whisper.... The housekeeper entered, a gaunt old woman, with\r\nher head bound up in a dark kerchief, and announced that dinner was\r\nready. All wended their way to the dining-room.\r\n\r\nThe dinner lasted for quite a long time. Ip\xc3\xa1toff kept a good cook, and\r\nordered pretty good wines, not from Moscow, but from the capital of the\r\ngovernment. Ip\xc3\xa1toff lived at his ease, as the saying goes. He did not\r\nown more than three hundred souls, but he was not in debt to any one,\r\nand had brought his estate into order. At table, the host himself did\r\nthe greater part of the talking; Eg\xc3\xb3r Kap\xc3\xadtonitch chimed in, but did not\r\nforget himself, at the same time; he ate and drank gloriously. M\xc3\xa1rya\r\nP\xc3\xa1vlovna preserved unbroken silence, only now and then replying with\r\nhalf-smiles to the hurried remarks of the two little girls, who sat one\r\non each side of her. They were, evidently, very fond of her. Vlad\xc3\xadmir\r\nSergy\xc3\xa9itch made several attempts to enter into conversation with her,\r\nbut without particular success. Folding Soul Bodryak\xc3\xb3ff even ate\r\nindolently and languidly. After dinner all went out on the terrace to\r\ndrink coffee. The weather was magnificent; from the garden was wafted\r\nthe sweet perfume of the lindens, which were then in full flower; the\r\nsummer air, slightly cooled by the thick shade of the trees, and the\r\nhumidity of the adjacent pond, breathed forth a sort of caressing\r\nwarmth. Suddenly, from behind the poplars of the dam, the trampling of a\r\nhorse\xe2\x80\x99s hoofs became audible, and a moment later, a horsewoman made her\r\nappearance in a long riding-habit and a grey hat, mounted on a bay\r\nhorse; she was riding at a gallop; a page was galloping behind her, on a\r\nsmall, white cob.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAh!\xe2\x80\x9d--exclaimed Ip\xc3\xa1toff,--\xe2\x80\x9cNad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna is coming. What a\r\npleasant surprise!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAlone?\xe2\x80\x9d--asked M\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna, who up to that moment had been standing\r\nmotionless in the doorway.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAlone.... Evidently, something has detained Pi\xc3\xb3tr Alexy\xc3\xa9evitch.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nM\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna darted a sidelong glance from beneath her brows, a flush\r\noverspread her face, and she turned away.\r\n\r\nIn the meantime, the horsewoman had ridden through the wicket-gate into\r\nthe garden, galloped up to the terrace, and sprang lightly to the\r\nground, without waiting either for her groom or for Ip\xc3\xa1toff, who had\r\nstarted to meet her. Briskly gathering up the train of her riding-habit,\r\nshe ran up the steps, and springing upon the terrace, exclaimed\r\nblithely:\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHere I am!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWelcome!\xe2\x80\x9d--said Ip\xc3\xa1toff.--\xe2\x80\x9cHow unexpected, how charming this is! Allow\r\nme to kiss your hand....\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cCertainly,\xe2\x80\x9d--returned the visitor; \xe2\x80\x9conly, you must pull off the glove\r\nyourself.--I cannot.\xe2\x80\x9d And, extending her hand to him, she nodded to\r\nM\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna.--\xe2\x80\x9cJust fancy, M\xc3\xa1sha, my brother will not be here\r\nto-day,\xe2\x80\x9d--she said, with a little sigh.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI see for myself that he is not here,\xe2\x80\x9d--replied M\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna in an\r\nundertone.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHe bade me say to thee that he is busy. Thou must not be angry. Good\r\nmorning, Eg\xc3\xb3r Kap\xc3\xadtonitch; good morning, Iv\xc3\xa1n \xc3\x8dlitch; good morning,\r\nchildren.... V\xc3\xa1sya,\xe2\x80\x9d--added the guest, turning to her small\r\ngroom,--\xe2\x80\x9corder them to walk Little Beauty up and down well, dost hear?\r\nM\xc3\xa1sha, please give me a pin, to fasten up my train.... Come here,\r\nMikha\xc3\xadl Nikol\xc3\xa1itch.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nIp\xc3\xa1toff went closer to her.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWho is that new person?\xe2\x80\x9d--she asked, quite loudly.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThat is a neighbour, Ast\xc3\xa1khoff, Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9evitch, you know, the\r\nowner of S\xc3\xa1sovo. I\xe2\x80\x99ll introduce him if you like, shall I?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cVery well ... afterward. Akh, what splendid weather!\xe2\x80\x9d--she went\r\non.--\xe2\x80\x9cEg\xc3\xb3r Kap\xc3\xadtonitch, tell me--can it be possible that Matry\xc3\xb3na\r\nM\xc3\xa1rkovna growls even in such weather as this?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cMatry\xc3\xb3na M\xc3\xa1rkovna never grumbles in any sort of weather, madam; and she\r\nis merely strict on the score of manners....\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd what are the Biri\xc3\xbaloff girls doing? They know all about it the next\r\nday, don\xe2\x80\x99t they?...\xe2\x80\x9d And she burst into a ringing, silvery laugh.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou are pleased to laugh constantly,\xe2\x80\x9d--returned Eg\xc3\xb3r\r\nKap\xc3\xadtonitch.--\xe2\x80\x9cHowever, when should a person laugh, if not at your age?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cEg\xc3\xb3r Kap\xc3\xadtonitch, don\xe2\x80\x99t get angry, my dear man! Akh, I\xe2\x80\x99m tired; allow\r\nme to sit down....\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nNad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna dropped into an arm-chair, and playfully pulled her\r\nhat down over her very eyes.\r\n\r\nIp\xc3\xa1toff led Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch up to her.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cPermit me, Nad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna, to present to you our neighbour, Mr.\r\nAst\xc3\xa1khoff, of whom you have, probably, heard a great deal.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nVlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch made his bow, while Nad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna looked up at\r\nhim from under the brim of her round hat.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna V\xc3\xa9retyeff, our neighbour,\xe2\x80\x9d--went on Ip\xc3\xa1toff,\r\nturning to Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch.--\xe2\x80\x9cShe lives here with her brother, Pi\xc3\xb3tr\r\nAlexy\xc3\xa9itch, a retired lieutenant of the Guards. She is a great friend of\r\nmy sister-in-law, and bears good will to our household in general.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cA whole formal inventory,\xe2\x80\x9d--said Nad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna, laughing, and, as\r\nbefore, scanning Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch from under her hat.\r\n\r\nBut, in the meantime, Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch was thinking to himself: \xe2\x80\x9cWhy,\r\nthis is a very pretty woman also.\xe2\x80\x9d And, in fact, Nad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna was\r\na very charming young girl. Slender and graceful, she appeared much\r\nyounger than she really was. She was already in her twenty-eighth year.\r\nShe had a round face, a small head, fluffy fair hair, a sharp, almost\r\naudaciously upturned little nose, and merry, almost crafty little eyes.\r\nMockery fairly glittered in them, and kindled in them in sparks. Her\r\nfeatures, extremely vivacious and mobile, sometimes assumed an almost\r\namusing expression; humour peered forth from them. Now and then, for the\r\nmost part suddenly, a shade of pensiveness flitted across her face,--and\r\nat such times it became gentle and kindly; but she could not surrender\r\nherself long to meditation. She easily seized upon the ridiculous sides\r\nof people, and drew very respectable caricatures. Everybody had petted\r\nher ever since she was born, and that is something which is immediately\r\nperceptible; people who have been spoiled in childhood preserve a\r\ncertain stamp to the end of their lives. Her brother loved her, although\r\nhe asserted that she stung, not like a bee, but like a wasp; because a\r\nbee stings and then dies, whereas it signifies nothing for a wasp to\r\nsting. This comparison enraged her.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHave you come here for long?\xe2\x80\x9d--she asked Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch, dropping\r\nher eyes, and twisting her riding-whip in her hands.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNo; I intend to go away from here to-morrow.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhither?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHome.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHome? Why, may I venture to ask?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat do you mean by \xe2\x80\x98why\xe2\x80\x99? I have affairs at home which do not brook\r\ndelay.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nNad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna looked at him.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAre you such a ... punctual man?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI try to be a punctual man,\xe2\x80\x9d--replied Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch.--\xe2\x80\x9cIn our\r\nsedate era, every honourable man _must_ be sedate and punctual.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThat is perfectly just,\xe2\x80\x9d--remarked Ip\xc3\xa1toff.--\xe2\x80\x9cIsn\xe2\x80\x99t that true Iv\xc3\xa1n\r\n\xc3\x8dlitch?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nIv\xc3\xa1n \xc3\x8dlitch merely glanced at Ip\xc3\xa1toff; but Eg\xc3\xb3r Kap\xc3\xadtonitch remarked:\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes, that\xe2\x80\x99s so.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9c\xe2\x80\x98Tis a pity,\xe2\x80\x9d--said Nad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna;--\xe2\x80\x9cprecisely what we lack is a\r\n_jeune premier_. You know how to act comedy, I suppose?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI have never put my powers in that line to the test.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI am convinced that you would act well. You have that sort of bearing\r\n... a stately mien, which is indispensable in a _jeune premier_. My\r\nbrother and I are preparing to set up a theatre here. However, we shall\r\nnot act comedies only: we shall act all sorts of things--dramas,\r\nballets, and even tragedies. Why wouldn\xe2\x80\x99t M\xc3\xa1sha do for Cleopatra or\r\nPh\xc3\xa8dre? Just look at her!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nVlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch turned round.... M\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna was gazing\r\nthoughtfully into the distance, as she stood leaning her head against\r\nthe door, with folded arms.... At that moment, her regular features\r\nreally did suggest the faces of ancient statues. She did not catch\r\nNad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna\xe2\x80\x99s last words; but, perceiving that the glances of\r\nall present were suddenly directed to her, she immediately divined what\r\nwas going on, blushed, and was about to retreat into the\r\ndrawing-room.... Nad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna briskly grasped her by the hand\r\nand, with the coquettish caressing action of a kitten, drew her toward\r\nher, and kissed that almost masculine hand. M\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna flushed more\r\nvividly than before.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThou art always playing pranks, N\xc3\xa1dya,\xe2\x80\x9d--she said.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDidn\xe2\x80\x99t I speak the truth about thee? I am ready to appeal to all....\r\nWell, enough, enough, I won\xe2\x80\x99t do it again. But I will say again,\xe2\x80\x9d--went\r\non Nad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna, addressing Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch,--\xe2\x80\x9cthat it is a\r\npity you are going away. We have a _jeune premier_, it is true; he calls\r\nhimself so, but he is very bad.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWho is he? permit me to inquire.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBodryak\xc3\xb3ff the poet. How can a poet be a _jeune premier_? In the first\r\nplace, he dresses in the most frightful way; in the second place, he\r\nwrites epigrams, and gets shy in the presence of every woman, even in\r\nmine. He lisps, one of his hands is always higher than his head, and I\r\ndon\xe2\x80\x99t know what besides. Tell me, please, M\xe2\x80\x99sieu Ast\xc3\xa1khoff, are all\r\npoets like that?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nVlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch drew himself up slightly.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI have never known a single one of them, personally; but I must confess\r\nthat I have never sought acquaintance with them.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes, you certainly are a positive man. We shall have to take\r\nBodryak\xc3\xb3ff; there\xe2\x80\x99s nothing else to be done. Other _jeunes premiers_ are\r\neven worse. That one, at all events, will learn his part by heart.\r\nM\xc3\xa1sha, in addition to tragic r\xc3\xb4les, will fill the post of prima\r\ndonna.... You haven\xe2\x80\x99t heard her sing, have you, M\xe2\x80\x99sieu Ast\xc3\xa1khoff?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNo,\xe2\x80\x9d--replied Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch, displaying his teeth in a smile;\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cand I did not know....\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat is the matter with thee to-day, N\xc3\xa1dya?\xe2\x80\x9d--said M\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna, with\r\na look of displeasure.\r\n\r\nNad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna sprang to her feet.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cFor Heaven\xe2\x80\x99s sake, M\xc3\xa1sha, do sing us something, please.... I won\xe2\x80\x99t let\r\nthee alone until thou singest us something, M\xc3\xa1sha dearest. I would sing\r\nmyself, to entertain the visitors, but thou knowest what a bad voice I\r\nhave. But, on the other hand, thou shalt see how splendidly I will\r\naccompany thee.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nM\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna made no reply.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThere\xe2\x80\x99s no getting rid of thee,\xe2\x80\x9d--she said at last.--\xe2\x80\x9cLike a spoiled\r\nchild, thou art accustomed to have all thy caprices humoured. I will\r\nsing, if you like.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBravo, bravo!\xe2\x80\x9d--exclaimed Nad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna, clapping her\r\nhands.--\xe2\x80\x9cLet us go into the drawing-room, gentlemen.--And as for\r\ncaprices,\xe2\x80\x9d--she added, laughing,--\xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99ll pay you off for that! Is it\r\npermissible to expose my weaknesses in the presence of strangers? Eg\xc3\xb3r\r\nKap\xc3\xadtonitch, does Matry\xc3\xb3na M\xc3\xa1rkovna shame you _thus_ before people?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cMatry\xc3\xb3na M\xc3\xa1rkovna,\xe2\x80\x9d--muttered Eg\xc3\xb3r Kap\xc3\xadtonitch,--\xe2\x80\x9cis a very worthy\r\nlady; only, on the score of manners....\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWell, come along, come along!\xe2\x80\x9d--Nad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna interrupted him,\r\nand entered the drawing-room.\r\n\r\nAll followed her. She tossed off her hat and seated herself at the\r\npiano. M\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna stood near the wall, a good way from Nad\xc3\xa9zhda\r\nAlexy\xc3\xa9evna.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cM\xc3\xa1sha,\xe2\x80\x9d--said the latter, after reflecting a little,--\xe2\x80\x9csing us \xe2\x80\x98The\r\nfarm-hand is sowing the grain.\xe2\x80\x99\xe2\x80\x9d[18]\r\n\r\nM\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna began to sing. Her voice was pure and powerful, and she\r\nsang well--simply, and without affectation. All listened to her with\r\ngreat attention, while Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch could not conceal his\r\namazement. When M\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna had finished, he stepped up to her, and\r\nbegan to assure her that he had not in the least expected....\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWait, there\xe2\x80\x99s something more coming!\xe2\x80\x9d--Nad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna interrupted\r\nhim.--\xe2\x80\x9cM\xc3\xa1sha, I will soothe thy Topknot[19] soul:--Now sing us \xe2\x80\x98Humming,\r\nhumming in the trees.\xe2\x80\x99\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAre you a Little Russian?\xe2\x80\x9d--Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch asked her.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI am a native of Little Russia,\xe2\x80\x9d she replied, and began to sing\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHumming, humming.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nAt first she uttered the words in an indifferent manner; but the\r\nmournfully passionate lay of her fatherland gradually began to stir her,\r\nher cheeks flushed scarlet, her glance flashed, her voice rang out\r\nfervently. She finished.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cGood heavens! How well thou hast sung that!\xe2\x80\x9d--said Nad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna,\r\nbending over the keys.--\xe2\x80\x9cWhat a pity that my brother was not here!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nM\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna instantly dropped her eyes, and laughed with her\r\ncustomary bitter little laugh.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou must give us something more,\xe2\x80\x9d--remarked Ip\xc3\xa1toff.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes, if you will be so good,\xe2\x80\x9d--added Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cExcuse me, I will not sing any more to-day,\xe2\x80\x9d--said M\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna, and\r\nleft the room.\r\n\r\nNad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna gazed after her, first reflected, then smiled, began\r\nto pick out \xe2\x80\x9cThe farm-hand is sowing the grain\xe2\x80\x9d with one finger, then\r\nsuddenly began to play a brilliant polka, and without finishing it,\r\nstruck a loud chord, clapped to the lid of the piano, and rose.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9c\xe2\x80\x98Tis a pity that there is no one to dance with!\xe2\x80\x9d--she exclaimed.--\xe2\x80\x9cIt\r\nwould be just the thing!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nVlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch approached her.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat a magnificent voice M\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna has,\xe2\x80\x9d--he remarked;--\xe2\x80\x9cand with\r\nhow much feeling she sings!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd are you fond of music?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes ... very.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cSuch a learned man, and you are fond of music!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBut what makes you think that I am learned?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAkh, yes; excuse me, I am always forgetting that you are a positive\r\nman. But where has M\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna gone? Wait, I\xe2\x80\x99ll go after her.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nAnd Nad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna fluttered out of the drawing-room.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cA giddy-pate, as you see,\xe2\x80\x9d--said Ip\xc3\xa1toff, coming up to Vlad\xc3\xadmir\r\nSergy\xc3\xa9itch;--\xe2\x80\x9cbut the kindest heart. And what an education she received\r\nyou cannot imagine; she can express herself in all languages. Well, they\r\nare wealthy people, so that is comprehensible.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes,\xe2\x80\x9d--articulated Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch, abstractedly,--\xe2\x80\x9cshe is a very\r\ncharming girl. But permit me to inquire, Was your wife also a native of\r\nLittle Russia?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes, she was, sir, My late wife was a Little Russian, as her sister\r\nM\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna is. My wife, to tell the truth, did not even have a\r\nperfectly pure pronunciation; although she was a perfect mistress of\r\nthe Russian language, still she did not express herself quite correctly;\r\nthey pronounce _i_, _ui_, there, and their _kha_ and _zhe_ are peculiar\r\nalso, you know; well, M\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna left her native land in early\r\nchildhood. But the Little Russian blood is still perceptible, isn\xe2\x80\x99t it?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cM\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna sings wonderfully,\xe2\x80\x9d--remarked Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cReally, it is not bad. But why don\xe2\x80\x99t they bring us some tea? And where\r\nhave the young ladies gone? \xe2\x80\x99Tis time to drink tea.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nThe young ladies did not return very speedily. In the meantime, the\r\nsamov\xc3\xa1r was brought, the table was laid for tea. Ip\xc3\xa1toff sent for them.\r\nBoth came in together. M\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna seated herself at the table to\r\npour the tea, while Nad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna walked to the door opening on\r\nthe terrace, and began to gaze out into the garden. The brilliant summer\r\nday had been succeeded by a clear, calm evening; the sunset was flaming;\r\nthe broad pond, half flooded with its crimson, stood a motionless\r\nmirror, grandly reflecting in its deep bosom all the airy depths of the\r\nsky, and the house, and the trees turned upside down, and had grown\r\nblack, as it were. Everything was silent round about. There was no noise\r\nanywhere.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cLook, how beautiful!\xe2\x80\x9d--said Nad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna to Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch,\r\nas he approached her;--\xe2\x80\x9cdown below there, in the pond, a star has\r\nkindled its fire by the side of the light in the house; the house-light\r\nis red, the other is golden. And yonder comes grandmamma,\xe2\x80\x9d--she added in\r\na loud voice.\r\n\r\nFrom behind a clump of lilac-bushes a small calash made its appearance.\r\nTwo men were drawing it. In it sat an old lady, all wrapped up, all\r\ndoubled over, with her head resting on her breast. The ruffle of her\r\nwhite cap almost completely concealed her withered and contracted little\r\nface. The tiny calash halted in front of the terrace. Ip\xc3\xa1toff emerged\r\nfrom the drawing-room, and his little daughters ran out after him. They\r\nhad been constantly slipping from room to room all the evening, like\r\nlittle mice.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI wish you good evening, dear mother,\xe2\x80\x9d--said Ip\xc3\xa1toff, stepping up close\r\nto the old woman, and elevating his voice.--\xe2\x80\x9cHow do you feel?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI have come to take a look at you,\xe2\x80\x9d--said the old woman in a dull\r\nvoice, and with an effort.--\xe2\x80\x9cWhat a glorious evening it is. I have been\r\nasleep all day, and now my feet have begun to ache. Okh, those feet of\r\nmine! They don\xe2\x80\x99t serve me, but they ache.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cPermit me, dear mother, to present to you our neighbour, Ast\xc3\xa1khoff,\r\nVlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI am very glad to meet you,\xe2\x80\x9d--returned the old woman, scanning him with\r\nher large, black, but dim-sighted eyes.--\xe2\x80\x9cI beg that you will love my\r\nson. He is a fine man; I gave him what education I could; of course, I\r\ndid the best a woman could. He is still somewhat flighty, but, God\r\nwilling, he will grow steady, and \xe2\x80\x99tis high time he did; \xe2\x80\x99tis time for\r\nme to surrender matters to him. Is that you, N\xc3\xa1dya?\xe2\x80\x9d--added the old\r\nwoman, glancing at Nad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes, grandmamma.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd is M\xc3\xa1sha pouring tea?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes, grandmamma, she is pouring tea.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd who else is there?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIv\xc3\xa1n \xc3\x8dlitch, and Eg\xc3\xb3r Kap\xc3\xadtonitch.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThe husband of Matry\xc3\xb3na M\xc3\xa1rkovna?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes, dear mother.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nThe old woman mumbled with her lips.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWell, good. But why is it, M\xc3\xadsha, that I can\xe2\x80\x99t manage to get hold of\r\nthe overseer? Order him to come to me very early to-morrow morning; I\r\nshall have a great deal of business to arrange with him. I see that\r\nnothing goes as it should with you, without me. Come, that will do, I am\r\ntired; take me away.... Farewell, b\xc3\xa1tiushka;[20] I don\xe2\x80\x99t remember your\r\nname and patronymic,\xe2\x80\x9d--she added, addressing Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch.\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cPardon an old woman. But don\xe2\x80\x99t come with me, grandchildren, it isn\xe2\x80\x99t\r\nnecessary. All you care for is to run all the time. M\xc3\xa1sha spoils you.\r\nWell, start on.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nThe old woman\xe2\x80\x99s head, which she had raised with difficulty, fell back\r\nagain on her breast....\r\n\r\nThe tiny calash started, and rolled softly away.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHow old is your mother?\xe2\x80\x9d--inquired Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOnly in her seventy-third year; but it is twenty-six years since her\r\nlegs failed her; that happened soon after the demise of my late father.\r\nBut she used to be a beauty.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nAll remained silent for a while.\r\n\r\nSuddenly, Nad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna gave a start. \xe2\x80\x9cWas that--a bat flying\r\npast? \xc3\x81\xc3\xaf, what a fright!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nAnd she hastily returned to the drawing-room.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt is time for me to go home, Mikha\xc3\xadl Nikol\xc3\xa1itch; order my horse to be\r\nsaddled.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd it is time for me to be going, too,\xe2\x80\x9d--remarked Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhere are you going?\xe2\x80\x9d--said Ip\xc3\xa1toff.--\xe2\x80\x9cSpend the night here. Nad\xc3\xa9zhda\r\nAlexy\xc3\xa9evna has only two versts to ride, while you have fully twelve. And\r\nwhat\xe2\x80\x99s your hurry, too, Nad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna? Wait for the moon; it will\r\nsoon be up now. It will be lighter to ride.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cVery well,\xe2\x80\x9d--said Nad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna.--\xe2\x80\x9cIt is a long time since I had\r\na moonlight ride.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd will you spend the night?\xe2\x80\x9d--Ip\xc3\xa1toff asked Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cReally, I don\xe2\x80\x99t know.... However, if I do not incommode you....\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNot in the least, I assure you; I will immediately order a chamber to\r\nbe prepared for you.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBut it is nice to ride by moonlight,\xe2\x80\x9d--began Nad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna, as\r\nsoon as candles were brought, tea was served, and Ip\xc3\xa1toff and Eg\xc3\xb3r\r\nKap\xc3\xadtonitch had sat down to play preference together, while The Folding\r\nSoul seated himself silently beside them:--\xe2\x80\x9cespecially through the\r\nforest, between the walnut-trees. It is both terrifying and agreeable,\r\nand what a strange play of light and shade there is--it always seems as\r\nthough some one were stealing up behind you, or in front of you....\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nVlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch smirked condescendingly.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd here\xe2\x80\x99s another thing,\xe2\x80\x9d--she went on;--\xe2\x80\x9chave you ever happened to\r\nsit beside the forest on a warm, dark, tranquil night? At such times it\r\nalways seems to me as though two persons were hotly disputing in an\r\nalmost inaudible whisper, behind me, close at my very ear.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThat is the blood beating,\xe2\x80\x9d--said Ip\xc3\xa1toff.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou describe in a very poetical way,\xe2\x80\x9d--remarked Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch.\r\nNad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna glanced at him.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDo you think so?... In that case, my description would not please\r\nM\xc3\xa1sha.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhy? Is not M\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna fond of poetry?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNo; she thinks all that sort of thing is made up--is all false; and she\r\ndoes not like that.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cA strange reproach!\xe2\x80\x9d--exclaimed Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch. \xe2\x80\x9cMade up! How\r\ncould it be otherwise? But, after all, what are composers for?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWell, there, that\xe2\x80\x99s exactly the point; but I am sure you cannot be fond\r\nof poetry.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOn the contrary, I love good verses, when they really are good and\r\nmelodious, and--how shall I say it?--when they present ideas,\r\nthoughts....\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nM\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna rose.\r\n\r\nNad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna turned swiftly toward her.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhither art thou going, M\xc3\xa1sha?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cTo put the children to bed. It is almost nine o\xe2\x80\x99clock.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBut cannot they go to bed without thee?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nBut M\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna took the children by the hand and went away with\r\nthem.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cShe is out of sorts to-day,\xe2\x80\x9d--remarked Nad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna;--\xe2\x80\x9cand I\r\nknow why,\xe2\x80\x9d--she added in an undertone.--\xe2\x80\x9cBut it will pass off.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAllow me to inquire,\xe2\x80\x9d--began Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch,--\xe2\x80\x9cwhere you intend to\r\nspend the winter?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cPerhaps here, perhaps in Petersburg. It seems to me that I shall be\r\nbored in Petersburg.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIn Petersburg! Good gracious! How is that possible?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nAnd Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch began to describe all the comforts, advantages,\r\nand charm of life in our capital. Nad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna listened to him\r\nwith attention, never taking her eyes from him. She seemed to be\r\ncommitting his features to memory, and laughed to herself from time to\r\ntime.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI see that you are very eloquent,\xe2\x80\x9d--she said at last.--\xe2\x80\x9cI shall be\r\nobliged to spend the winter in Petersburg.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou will not repent of it,\xe2\x80\x9d--remarked Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI never repent of anything; it is not worth the bother. If you have\r\nperpetrated a blunder, try to forget it as speedily as possible--that\xe2\x80\x99s\r\nall.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAllow me to ask,\xe2\x80\x9d--began Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch, after a brief pause, and\r\nin the French language;--\xe2\x80\x9chave you known M\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna long?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAllow me to ask,\xe2\x80\x9d--retorted Nad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna, with a swift\r\nlaugh;--\xe2\x80\x9cwhy you have put precisely that question to me in French?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBecause ... for no particular reason....\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nAgain Nad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna laughed.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNo; I have not known her very long. But she is a remarkable girl, isn\xe2\x80\x99t\r\nshe?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cShe is very original,\xe2\x80\x9d--said Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch, through his teeth.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd in your mouth--in the mouth of positive persons--does that\r\nconstitute praise? I do not think so. Perhaps I seem original to you,\r\nalso? But,\xe2\x80\x9d--she added, rising from her seat and casting a glance\r\nthrough the window,--\xe2\x80\x9cthe moon must have risen; that is its light on the\r\npoplars. It is time to depart.... I will go and give order that Little\r\nBeauty shall be saddled.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHe is already saddled, ma\xe2\x80\x99am,\xe2\x80\x9d--said Nad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna\xe2\x80\x99s groom,\r\nstepping out from the shadow in the garden into a band of light which\r\nfell on the terrace.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAh! Well, that\xe2\x80\x99s very good, indeed! M\xc3\xa1sha, where art thou? Come and bid\r\nme good-bye.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nM\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna made her appearance from the adjoining room. The men rose\r\nfrom the card-table.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cSo you are going already?\xe2\x80\x9d--inquired Ip\xc3\xa1toff.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI am; it is high time.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nShe approached the door leading into the garden.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat a night!\xe2\x80\x9d--she exclaimed.--\xe2\x80\x9cCome here; hold out your face to it;\r\ndo you feel how it seems to breathe upon you? And what fragrance! all\r\nthe flowers have waked up now. They have waked up--and we are preparing\r\nto go to sleep.... Ah, by the way, M\xc3\xa1sha,\xe2\x80\x9d--she added:--\xe2\x80\x9cI have told\r\nVlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch, you know, that thou art not fond of poetry. And\r\nnow, farewell ... yonder comes my horse....\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nAnd she ran briskly down the steps of the terrace, swung herself lightly\r\ninto the saddle, said, \xe2\x80\x9cGood-bye until to-morrow!\xe2\x80\x9d--and lashing her\r\nhorse on the neck with her riding-switch, she galloped off in the\r\ndirection of the dam.... The groom set off at a trot after her.\r\n\r\nAll gazed after her....\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cUntil to-morrow!\xe2\x80\x9d--her voice rang out once more from behind the\r\npoplars.\r\n\r\nThe hoof-beats were still audible for a long time in the silence of the\r\nsummer night. At last, Ip\xc3\xa1toff proposed that they should go into the\r\nhouse again.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt really is very nice out of doors,\xe2\x80\x9d--he said;--\xe2\x80\x9cbut we must finish\r\nour game.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nAll obeyed him.
