Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch began to question M\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna as\r\nto why she did not like poetry.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cVerses do not please me,\xe2\x80\x9d--she returned, with apparent reluctance.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBut perhaps you have not read many verses?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI have not read them myself, but I have had them read to me.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd is it possible that they did not please you?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNo; none of them.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNot even P\xc3\xbashkin\xe2\x80\x99s verses?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNot even P\xc3\xbashkin\xe2\x80\x99s.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhy?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nM\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna made no answer; but Ip\xc3\xa1toff, twisting round across the\r\nback of his chair, remarked, with a good-natured laugh, that she not\r\nonly did not like verses, but sugar also, and, in general, could not\r\nendure anything sweet.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBut, surely, there are verses which are not sweet,\xe2\x80\x9d--retorted Vlad\xc3\xadmir\r\nSergy\xc3\xa9itch.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cFor example?\xe2\x80\x9d--M\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna asked him.\r\n\r\nVlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch scratched behind his ear.... He himself knew very\r\nfew verses by heart, especially of the sort which were not sweet.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhy, here now,\xe2\x80\x9d--he exclaimed at last;--\xe2\x80\x9cdo you know P\xc3\xbashkin\xe2\x80\x99s \xe2\x80\x98The\r\nUpas-Tree\xe2\x80\x99?[21] No? That poem cannot possibly be called sweet.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cRecite it,\xe2\x80\x9d--said M\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna, dropping her eyes.\r\n\r\nVlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch first stared at the ceiling, frowned, mumbled\r\nsomething to himself, and at last recited \xe2\x80\x9cThe Upas-Tree.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nAfter the first four lines, M\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna slowly raised her eyes, and\r\nwhen Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch ended, she said, with equal slowness:\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cPlease recite it again.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cSo these verses do please you?\xe2\x80\x9d--asked Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cRecite it again.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nVlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch repeated \xe2\x80\x9cThe Upas-Tree.\xe2\x80\x9d M\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna rose, went\r\nout into the next room, and returned with a sheet of paper, an inkstand\r\nand a pen.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cPlease write that down for me,\xe2\x80\x9d--she said to Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cCertainly; with pleasure,\xe2\x80\x9d--he replied, beginning to write.--\xe2\x80\x9cBut I\r\nmust confess that I am puzzled to know why these verses have pleased you\r\nso. I recited them simply to prove to you that not all verses are\r\nsweet.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cSo am I!\xe2\x80\x9d--exclaimed Ip\xc3\xa1toff.--\xe2\x80\x9cWhat do you think of those verses, Iv\xc3\xa1n\r\n\xc3\x8dlitch?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nIv\xc3\xa1n \xc3\x8dlitch, according to his wont, merely glanced at Ip\xc3\xa1toff, but did\r\nnot utter a word.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHere, ma\xe2\x80\x99am,--I have finished,\xe2\x80\x9d--said Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch, as he placed\r\nan interrogation-point at the end of the last line.\r\n\r\nM\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna thanked him, and carried the written sheet off to her own\r\nroom.\r\n\r\nHalf an hour later supper was served, and an hour later all the guests\r\ndispersed to their rooms. Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch had repeatedly addressed\r\nM\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna; but it was difficult to conduct a conversation with her,\r\nand his anecdotes did not seem to interest her greatly. He probably\r\nwould have fallen asleep as soon as he got into bed had he not been\r\nhindered by his neighbour, Eg\xc3\xb3r Kap\xc3\xadtonitch. Matry\xc3\xb3na M\xc3\xa1rkovna\xe2\x80\x99s\r\nhusband, after he was fully undressed and had got into bed, talked for a\r\nvery long time with his servant, and kept bestowing reprimands on him.\r\nEvery word he uttered was perfectly audible to Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch: only\r\na thin partition separated them.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHold the candle in front of thy breast,\xe2\x80\x9d--said Eg\xc3\xb3r Kap\xc3\xadtonitch, in a\r\nquerulous voice;--\xe2\x80\x9chold it so that I can see thy face. Thou hast aged\r\nme, aged me, thou conscienceless man--hast aged me completely.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBut, for mercy\xe2\x80\x99s sake, Eg\xc3\xb3r Kap\xc3\xadtonitch, how have I aged you?\xe2\x80\x9d--the\r\nservant\xe2\x80\x99s dull and sleepy voice made itself heard.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHow? I\xe2\x80\x99ll tell thee how. How many times have I said to thee: \xe2\x80\x98M\xc3\xadtka,\xe2\x80\x99 I\r\nhave said to thee, \xe2\x80\x98when thou goest a-visiting with me, always take two\r\ngarments of each sort, especially\xe2\x80\x99 ... hold the candle in front of thy\r\nbreast ... \xe2\x80\x98especially underwear.\xe2\x80\x99 And what hast thou done to me\r\nto-day?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat, sir?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9c\xe2\x80\x98What, sir?\xe2\x80\x99 What am I to put on to-morrow?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhy, the same things you wore to-day, sir.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThou hast aged me, malefactor, aged me. I was almost beside myself with\r\nthe heat to-day, as it was. Hold the candle in front of thy breast, I\r\ntell thee, and don\xe2\x80\x99t sleep when thy master is talking to thee.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWell, but Matry\xc3\xb3na M\xc3\xa1rkovna said, sir, \xe2\x80\x98That\xe2\x80\x99s enough. Why do you\r\nalways take such a mass of things with you? They only get worn out for\r\nnothing.\xe2\x80\x99\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cMatry\xc3\xb3na M\xc3\xa1rkovna.... Is it a woman\xe2\x80\x99s business, pray, to enter into\r\nthat? You have aged me. Okh, you have made me old before my time!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes; and Yakh\xc3\xadm said the same thing, sir.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat\xe2\x80\x99s that thou saidst?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI say, Yakh\xc3\xadm said the same thing, sir.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYakh\xc3\xadm! Yakh\xc3\xadm!\xe2\x80\x9d--repeated Eg\xc3\xb3r Kap\xc3\xadtonitch, reproachfully.--\xe2\x80\x9cEkh, you\r\nhave aged me, ye accursed, and don\xe2\x80\x99t even know how to speak Russian\r\nintelligibly. Yakh\xc3\xadm! Who\xe2\x80\x99s Yakh\xc3\xadm! Efr\xc3\xadm,--well, that might be allowed\r\nto pass, it is permissible to say that; because the genuine Greek name\r\nis Evth\xc3\xadmius, dost understand me?... Hold the candle in front of thy\r\nbreast.... So, for the sake of brevity, thou mayest say Efr\xc3\xadm, if thou\r\nwilt, but not Yakh\xc3\xadm by any manner of means. Y\xc3\xa1khim!\xe2\x80\x9d[22] added Eg\xc3\xb3r\r\nKap\xc3\xadtonitch, emphasising the syllable _Ya_.--\xe2\x80\x9cYou have aged me, ye\r\nmalefactors. Hold the candle in front of thy breast!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nAnd for a long time, Eg\xc3\xb3r Kap\xc3\xadtonitch continued to berate his servant,\r\nin spite of sighs, coughs, and other tokens of impatience on the part of\r\nVlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch....\r\n\r\nAt last he dismissed his M\xc3\xadtka, and fell asleep; but Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch\r\nwas no better off for that: Eg\xc3\xb3r Kap\xc3\xadtonitch snored so mightily and in\r\nso deep a voice, with such playful transitions from high tones to the\r\nvery lowest, with such accompanying whistlings, and even snappings, that\r\nit seemed as though the very partition were shaking in response to him;\r\npoor Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch almost wept. It was very stifling in the\r\nchamber which had been allotted to him, and the feather-bed whereon he\r\nwas lying embraced his whole body in a sort of crawling heat.\r\n\r\nAt last, in despair, Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch rose, opened the window, and\r\nbegan with avidity to inhale the nocturnal freshness. The window looked\r\nout on the park. It was light overhead, the round face of the full moon\r\nwas now clearly reflected in the pond, and stretched itself out in a\r\nlong, golden sheaf of slowly transfused spangles. On one of the paths\r\nVlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch espied a figure in woman\xe2\x80\x99s garb; he looked more\r\nintently; it was M\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna; in the moonlight her face seemed pale.\r\nShe stood motionless, and suddenly began to speak.... Vlad\xc3\xadmir\r\nSergy\xc3\xa9itch cautiously put out his head....\r\n\r\n    \xe2\x80\x9cBut a man--with glance imperious--\r\n     Sent a man to the Upas-tree....\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nreached his ear....\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cCome,\xe2\x80\x9d--he thought,--\xe2\x80\x9cthe verses must have taken effect....\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nAnd he began to listen with redoubled attention.... But M\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna\r\nspeedily fell silent, and turned her face more directly toward him; he\r\ncould distinguish her large, dark eyes, her severe brows and lips....\r\n\r\nSuddenly, she started, wheeled round, entered the shadow cast by a dense\r\nwall of lofty acacias, and disappeared. Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch stood for a\r\nconsiderable time at the window, then got into bed again, but did not\r\nfall asleep very soon.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cA strange being,\xe2\x80\x9d--he thought, as he tossed from side to side;--\xe2\x80\x9cand\r\nyet they say that there is nothing particular in the provinces.... The\r\nidea! A strange being! I shall ask her to-morrow what she was doing in\r\nthe park.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nAnd Eg\xc3\xb3r Kap\xc3\xadtonitch continued to snore as before.\r\n\r\n\r\nIII\r\n\r\nOn the following morning Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch awoke quite late, and\r\nimmediately after the general tea and breakfast in the dining-room,\r\ndrove off home to finish his business on his estate, in spite of all old\r\nIp\xc3\xa1toff\xe2\x80\x99s attempts to detain him. M\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna also was present at\r\nthe tea; but Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch did not consider it necessary to\r\nquestion her concerning her late stroll of the night before; he was one\r\nof the people who find it difficult to surrender themselves for two days\r\nin succession to any unusual thoughts and assumptions whatsoever. He\r\nwould have been obliged to discuss verses, and the so-called \xe2\x80\x9cpoetical\xe2\x80\x9d\r\nmood wearied him very quickly. He spent the whole day until dinner in\r\nthe fields, ate with great appetite, dozed off, and when he woke up,\r\ntried to take up the clerk\xe2\x80\x99s accounts; but before he had finished the\r\nfirst page, he ordered his tarant\xc3\xa1s to be harnessed, and set off for\r\nIp\xc3\xa1toff\xe2\x80\x99s. Evidently, even positive people do not bear about in their\r\nbreasts hearts of stone, and they are no more fond of being bored than\r\nother plain mortals.\r\n\r\nAs he drove upon the dam he heard voices and the sound of music. They\r\nwere singing Russian ballads in chorus in Ip\xc3\xa1toff\xe2\x80\x99s house. He found the\r\nwhole company which he had left in the morning on the terrace; all,\r\nNad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna among the rest, were sitting in a circle around a\r\nman of two-and-thirty--a swarthy-skinned, black-eyed, black-haired man\r\nin a velvet jacket, with a scarlet kerchief carelessly knotted about his\r\nneck, and a guitar in his hands. This was Pi\xc3\xb3tr Alexy\xc3\xa9evitch V\xc3\xa9retyeff,\r\nbrother of Nad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna. On catching sight of Vlad\xc3\xadmir\r\nSergy\xc3\xa9itch, old Ip\xc3\xa1toff advanced to meet him with a joyful cry, led him\r\nup to V\xc3\xa9retyeff, and introduced them to each other. After exchanging the\r\ncustomary greetings with his new acquaintance, Ast\xc3\xa1khoff made a\r\nrespectful bow to the latter\xe2\x80\x99s sister.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWe\xe2\x80\x99re singing songs in country fashion, Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch,\xe2\x80\x9d--began\r\nIp\xc3\xa1toff, and pointing to V\xc3\xa9retyeff he added:-\xe2\x80\x9cPi\xc3\xb3tr Alexy\xc3\xa9itch is our\r\nleader,--and what a leader! Just you listen to him!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThis is very pleasant,\xe2\x80\x9d--replied Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWill not you join the choir?\xe2\x80\x9d--Nad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna asked him.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI should be heartily glad to do so, but I have no voice.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThat doesn\xe2\x80\x99t matter! See, Eg\xc3\xb3r Kap\xc3\xadtonitch is singing, and I\xe2\x80\x99m singing.\r\nAll you have to do is to chime in. Pray, sit down; and do thou strike\r\nup, my dear fellow!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat song shall we sing now?\xe2\x80\x9d--said V\xc3\xa9retyeff, thrumming the guitar;\r\nand suddenly stopping short, he looked at M\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna, who was\r\nsitting by his side.--\xe2\x80\x9cI think it is your turn now,\xe2\x80\x9d--he said to her.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNo; do you sing,\xe2\x80\x9d--replied M\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHere\xe2\x80\x99s a song now: \xe2\x80\x98Adown dear Mother Volga\xe2\x80\x99\xe2\x80\x9d--said Vlad\xc3\xadmir\r\nSergy\xc3\xa9itch, with importance.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNo, we will save that up for the last,\xe2\x80\x9d--replied V\xc3\xa9retyeff, and\r\ntinkling the strings of the guitar, he struck up, in slow measure, \xe2\x80\x9cThe\r\nsun is setting.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nHe sang splendidly, dashingly, and blithely. His manly face, already\r\nexpressive, became still more animated when he sang; now and then he\r\nshrugged his shoulders, suddenly pressed the strings with his palm,\r\nraised his arm, shook his curls, and darted a falcon-like look around\r\nhim. More than once in Moscow he had seen the famous Ily\xc3\xa1, and he\r\nimitated him. The chorus chimed in lustily. M\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna\xe2\x80\x99s voice\r\nseparated itself in a melodious flood from the other voices; it seemed\r\nto drag them after it; but she would not sing alone, and V\xc3\xa9retyeff\r\nremained the leader to the end.\r\n\r\nThey sang a great many other songs....\r\n\r\nIn the meantime, along with the evening shadows, a thunder-storm drew\r\non. From noonday it had been steaming hot, and thunder had kept rumbling\r\nin the distance; but now a broad thunder-cloud, which had long lain like\r\na leaden pall on the very rim of the horizon, began to increase and show\r\nitself above the crests of the trees, the stifling air began to quiver\r\nmore distinctly, shaken more and more violently by the approaching\r\nstorm; the wind rose, rustled the foliage abruptly, died into silence,\r\nagain made a prolonged clamour, and began to roar; a surly gloom\r\nflitted over the earth, swiftly dispelling the last reflection of the\r\nsunset glow; dense clouds suddenly floated up, as though rending\r\nthemselves free, and sailed across the sky; a fine rain began to patter\r\ndown, the lightning flashed in a red flame, and the thunder rumbled\r\nheavily and angrily.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cLet us go,\xe2\x80\x9d--said old Ip\xc3\xa1toff,--\xe2\x80\x9cor we shall be drenched.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nAll rose.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDirectly!\xe2\x80\x9d--exclaimed Pi\xc3\xb3tr Alexy\xc3\xa9itch.--\xe2\x80\x9cOne more song, the last.\r\nListen:\r\n\r\n    \xe2\x80\x9cAkh, thou house, thou house of mine,\r\n     Thou new house of mine....\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nhe struck up in a loud voice, briskly striking the strings of the guitar\r\nwith his whole hand. \xe2\x80\x9cMy new house of maple-wood,\xe2\x80\x9d joined in the chorus,\r\nas though reluctantly carried away. Almost at the same moment, the rain\r\nbegan to beat down in streams; but V\xc3\xa9retyeff sang \xe2\x80\x9cMy house\xe2\x80\x9d to the end.\r\nFrom time to time, drowned by the claps of thunder, the dashing ballad\r\nseemed more dashing than ever beneath the noisy rattle and gurgling of\r\nthe rain. At last the final detonation of the chorus rang out--and the\r\nwhole company ran, laughing, into the drawing-room. Loudest of all\r\nlaughed the little girls, Ip\xc3\xa1toff\xe2\x80\x99s daughters, as they shook the\r\nrain-drops from their frocks. But, by way of precaution, Ip\xc3\xa1toff closed\r\nthe window, and locked the door; and Eg\xc3\xb3r Kap\xc3\xadtonitch lauded him,\r\nremarking that Matry\xc3\xb3na M\xc3\xa1rkovna also always gave orders to shut up\r\nwhenever there was a thunder-storm, because electricity is more capable\r\nof acting in an empty space. Bodryak\xc3\xb3ff looked him straight in the face,\r\nstepped aside, and overturned a chair. Such trifling mishaps were\r\nconstantly happening to him.\r\n\r\nThe thunder-storm passed over very soon. The doors and windows were\r\nopened again, and the rooms were filled with moist fragrance. Tea was\r\nbrought. After tea the old men sat down to cards again. Iv\xc3\xa1n \xc3\x8dlitch\r\njoined them, as usual. Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch was about to go to M\xc3\xa1rya\r\nP\xc3\xa1vlovna, who was sitting at the window with V\xc3\xa9retyeff; but Nad\xc3\xa9zhda\r\nAlexy\xc3\xa9evna called him to her, and immediately entered into a fervent\r\ndiscussion with him about Petersburg and Petersburg life. She attacked\r\nit; Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch began to defend it. Nad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna appeared\r\nto be trying to keep him by her side.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat are you wrangling about?\xe2\x80\x9d--inquired V\xc3\xa9retyeff, rising and\r\napproaching them.\r\n\r\nHe swayed lazily from side to side as he walked; in all his movements\r\nthere was perceptible something which was not exactly carelessness, nor\r\nyet exactly fatigue.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cStill about Petersburg.\xe2\x80\x9d--replied Nad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna.--\xe2\x80\x9cVlad\xc3\xadmir\r\nSergy\xc3\xa9itch cannot sufficiently praise it.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9c\xe2\x80\x98Tis a fine town,\xe2\x80\x9d--remarked V\xc3\xa9retyeff;--\xe2\x80\x9cbut, in my opinion, it is\r\nnice everywhere. By Heaven, it is. If one only has two or three women,\r\nand--pardon my frankness--wine, a man really has nothing left to wish\r\nfor.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou surprise me,\xe2\x80\x9d--retorted Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch. \xe2\x80\x9cCan it be possible\r\nthat you are really of one opinion, that there does not exist for the\r\ncultured man....\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cPerhaps ... in fact ... I agree with you,\xe2\x80\x9d--interrupted V\xc3\xa9retyeff, who,\r\nnotwithstanding all his courtesy, had a habit of not listening to the\r\nend of retorts;--\xe2\x80\x9cbut that\xe2\x80\x99s not in my line; I\xe2\x80\x99m not a philosopher.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNeither am I a philosopher,\xe2\x80\x9d--replied Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch;--\xe2\x80\x9cand I have\r\nnot the slightest desire to be one; but here it is a question of\r\nsomething entirely different.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nV\xc3\xa9retyeff cast an abstracted glance at his sister, and she, with a faint\r\nlaugh, bent toward him, and whispered in a low voice:\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cPetr\xc3\xbasha, my dear, imitate Eg\xc3\xb3r Kap\xc3\xadtonitch for us, please.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nV\xc3\xa9retyeff\xe2\x80\x99s face instantly changed, and, Heaven knows by what miracle,\r\nbecame remarkably like the face of Eg\xc3\xb3r Kap\xc3\xadtonitch, although the\r\nfeatures of the two faces had absolutely nothing in common, and\r\nV\xc3\xa9retyeff himself barely wrinkled up his nose and pulled down the\r\ncorners of his lips.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOf course,\xe2\x80\x9d--he began to whisper, in a voice which was the exact\r\ncounterpart of Eg\xc3\xb3r Kap\xc3\xadtonitch\xe2\x80\x99s,--\xe2\x80\x9cMatry\xc3\xb3na M\xc3\xa1rkovna is a severe lady\r\non the score of manners; but, on the other hand, she is a model wife. It\r\nis true that no matter what I may have said....\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThe Biri\xc3\xbaloff girls know it all,\xe2\x80\x9d--put in Nad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna, hardly\r\nrestraining her laughter.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cEverything is known on the following day,\xe2\x80\x9d--replied V\xc3\xa9retyeff, with\r\nsuch a comical grimace, with such a perturbed sidelong glance, that even\r\nVlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch burst out laughing.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI see that you possess great talent for mimicry,\xe2\x80\x9d--he remarked.\r\n\r\nV\xc3\xa9retyeff passed his hand over his face, his features resumed their\r\nordinary expression, while Nad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna exclaimed:\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOh, yes! he can mimic any one whom he wishes.... He\xe2\x80\x99s a master hand at\r\nthat.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd would you be able to imitate me, for example?\xe2\x80\x9d--inquired Vlad\xc3\xadmir\r\nSergy\xc3\xa9itch.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI should think so!\xe2\x80\x9d--returned Nad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna:--\xe2\x80\x9cof course.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAkh, pray do me the favour to represent me,\xe2\x80\x9d--said Ast\xc3\xa1khoff, turning\r\nto V\xc3\xa9retyeff.--\xe2\x80\x9cI beg that you will not stand on ceremony.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd so you too have believed her?\xe2\x80\x9d--replied V\xc3\xa9retyeff, slightly\r\nscrewing up one eye, and imparting to his voice the sound of\r\nAst\xc3\xa1khoff\xe2\x80\x99s voice, but so cautiously and slightly that only Nad\xc3\xa9zhda\r\nAlexy\xc3\xa9evna noticed it, and bit her lips.--\xe2\x80\x9cPlease do not believe her;\r\nshe will tell you other untrue things about me.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd if you only knew what an actor he is!\xe2\x80\x9d--pursued Nad\xc3\xa9zhda\r\nAlexy\xc3\xa9evna:--\xe2\x80\x9che plays every conceivable sort of a part. And so\r\nsplendidly! He is our stage-manager, and our prompter, and everything\r\nyou like. It\xe2\x80\x99s a pity that you are going away so soon.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cSister, thy partiality blinds thee,\xe2\x80\x9d--remarked V\xc3\xa9retyeff, in a pompous\r\ntone, but still with the same touch of Ast\xc3\xa1khoff.--\xe2\x80\x9cWhat will Mr.\r\nAst\xc3\xa1khoff think of thee?--He will regard thee as a rustic.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNo, indeed,\xe2\x80\x9d--Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch was beginning....\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cSee here, Petr\xc3\xbasha,\xe2\x80\x9d--interposed Nad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna;--\xe2\x80\x9cplease show us\r\nhow a drunken man is utterly unable to get his handkerchief out of his\r\npocket; or no: show us, rather, how a boy catches a fly on the window,\r\nand how it buzzes under his fingers.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThou art a regular child,\xe2\x80\x9d--replied V\xc3\xa9retyeff.\r\n\r\nNevertheless he rose, and stepping to the window, beside which M\xc3\xa1rya\r\nP\xc3\xa1vlovna was sitting, he began to pass his hand across the panes, and\r\nrepresent how a small boy catches a fly.\r\n\r\nThe accuracy with which he imitated its pitiful squeak was really\r\namazing. It seemed as though a live fly were actually struggling under\r\nhis fingers. Nad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna burst out laughing, and gradually every\r\none in the room got to laughing. M\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna\xe2\x80\x99s face alone underwent\r\nno change, not even her lips quivered. She sat with downcast eyes, but\r\nraised them at last, and casting a serious glance at V\xc3\xa9retyeff, she\r\nmuttered through her set teeth:\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat possesses you to make a clown of yourself?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nV\xc3\xa9retyeff instantly turned away from the window, and, after standing\r\nstill for a moment in the middle of the room, he went out on the\r\nterrace, and thence into the garden, which had already grown perfectly\r\ndark.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHow amusing that Pi\xc3\xb3tr Alexy\xc3\xa9itch is!\xe2\x80\x9d--exclaimed Eg\xc3\xb3r Kap\xc3\xadtonitch,\r\nslapping down the seven of trumps with a flourish on some one else\xe2\x80\x99s\r\nace.--\xe2\x80\x9cReally, he\xe2\x80\x99s very amusing!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nNad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna rose, and hastily approaching M\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna, asked\r\nher in an undertone:\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat didst thou say to my brother?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNothing,\xe2\x80\x9d--replied the other.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat dost thou mean by \xe2\x80\x98nothing\xe2\x80\x99? Impossible.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nAnd after waiting a little, Nad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna said: \xe2\x80\x9cCome!\xe2\x80\x9d--took\r\nM\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna by the hand, forced her to rise, and went off with her\r\ninto the garden.\r\n\r\nVlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch gazed after the two young girls not without\r\nperplexity. But they were not absent long; a quarter of an hour later\r\nthey returned, and Pi\xc3\xb3tr Alexy\xc3\xa9itch entered the room with them.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat a splendid night!\xe2\x80\x9d exclaimed Nad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna, as she\r\nentered.--\xe2\x80\x9cHow beautiful it is in the garden!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAkh, yes. By the way,\xe2\x80\x9d--said Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch;--\xe2\x80\x9callow me to\r\ninquire, M\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna, whether it was you whom I saw in the garden\r\nlast night?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nM\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna gave him a swift look straight in the eyes.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cMoreover, so far as I could make out, you were declaiming P\xc3\xbashkin\xe2\x80\x99s\r\n\xe2\x80\x98The Upas-Tree.\xe2\x80\x99\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nV\xc3\xa9retyeff frowned slightly, and he also began to stare at Ast\xc3\xa1khoff.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt really was I,\xe2\x80\x9d--said M\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna;--\xe2\x80\x9conly, I was not declaiming\r\nanything; I never declaim.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cPerhaps it seemed so to me,\xe2\x80\x9d--began Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch;--\xe2\x80\x9cbut....\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt did seem so to you?\xe2\x80\x9d--remarked M\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna, coldly.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat\xe2\x80\x99s \xe2\x80\x98The Upas-Tree\xe2\x80\x99?\xe2\x80\x9d--inquired Nad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhy, don\xe2\x80\x99t you know?\xe2\x80\x9d--retorted Ast\xc3\xa1khoff.--\xe2\x80\x9cDo you mean to say you\r\ndon\xe2\x80\x99t remember P\xc3\xbashkin\xe2\x80\x99s verses: \xe2\x80\x98On the unhealthy, meagre soil\xe2\x80\x99?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cSomehow I don\xe2\x80\x99t remember.... That upas-tree is a poisonous tree, isn\xe2\x80\x99t\r\nit?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cLike the datura.... Dost remember, M\xc3\xa1sha, how beautiful the datura were\r\non our balcony, in the moonlight, with their long, white blossoms? Dost\r\nremember what fragrance poured from them,--so sweet, insinuating, and\r\ninsidious?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAn insidious fragrance!\xe2\x80\x9d--exclaimed Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes; insidious. What are you surprised at? They say it is dangerous,\r\nbut it is attractive. Why can evil attract? Evil should not be\r\nbeautiful.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOh, what theories!\xe2\x80\x9d--remarked Pi\xc3\xb3tr Alexy\xc3\xa9itch;--\xe2\x80\x9chow far away we have\r\ngot from verses!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI recited those verses yesterday evening to M\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna,\xe2\x80\x9d interposed\r\nVlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch;--\xe2\x80\x9cand they pleased her greatly.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAkh, please recite them,\xe2\x80\x9d--said Nad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cCertainly, madam.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nAnd Ast\xc3\xa1khoff recited \xe2\x80\x9cThe Upas-Tree.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cToo bombastic,\xe2\x80\x9d--ejaculated V\xc3\xa9retyeff, as though against his will, as\r\nsoon as Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch had finished.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThe poem is too bombastic?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNo, not the poem.... Excuse me, it seems to me that you do not recite\r\nwith sufficient simplicity. The thing speaks for itself; however, I may\r\nbe mistaken.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNo, thou art not mistaken,\xe2\x80\x9d--said Nad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna, pausing between\r\nher words.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOh, yes; that is a matter of course! In thy eyes I am a genius, an\r\nextremely gifted man, who knows everything, can do everything;\r\nunfortunately, he is overcome with laziness; isn\xe2\x80\x99t that so?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nNad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna merely shook her head.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI shall not quarrel with you; you must know best about that,\xe2\x80\x9d--remarked\r\nVlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch, somewhat sulkily.--\xe2\x80\x9cThat\xe2\x80\x99s not in my line.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI made a mistake, pardon me,\xe2\x80\x9d--ejaculated V\xc3\xa9retyeff, hastily.\r\n\r\nIn the meantime, the game of cards had come to an end.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAkh, by the way,\xe2\x80\x9d--said Ip\xc3\xa1toff, as he rose;--\xe2\x80\x9cVlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch, one\r\nof the local landed proprietors, a neighbour, a very fine and worthy\r\nman, Ak\xc3\xadlin, Gavr\xc3\xadla Step\xc3\xa1nitch, has commissioned me to ask you whether\r\nyou will not do him the honour to be present at his ball,--that is, I\r\njust put it so, for beauty of style, and said \xe2\x80\x98ball,\xe2\x80\x99 but it is only an\r\nevening party with dancing, quite informal. He would have called upon\r\nyou himself without fail, only he was afraid of disturbing you.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI am much obliged to the gentleman,\xe2\x80\x9d--returned Vlad\xc3\xadmir\r\nSergy\xc3\xa9itch;--\xe2\x80\x9cbut it is imperatively necessary that I should return\r\nhome....\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhy--but when do you suppose the ball takes place? \xe2\x80\x99Tis to-morrow.\r\nTo-morrow is Gavr\xc3\xadla Step\xc3\xa1nitch\xe2\x80\x99s Name-day. One day more won\xe2\x80\x99t matter,\r\nand how much pleasure you will give him! And it\xe2\x80\x99s only ten versts from\r\nhere. If you will allow, we will take you thither.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cReally, I don\xe2\x80\x99t know,\xe2\x80\x9d--began Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch.--\xe2\x80\x9cAnd are you\r\ngoing?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThe whole family! And Nad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna and Pi\xc3\xb3tr\r\nAlexy\xc3\xa9itch,--everybody is going!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou may invite me on the spot for the fifth quadrille, if you\r\nlike,\xe2\x80\x9d--remarked Nad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna.--\xe2\x80\x9cThe first four are already\r\nbespoken.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou are very kind; and are you already engaged for the mazurka?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI? Let me think ... no, I think I am not.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIn that case, if you will be so kind, I should like to have the\r\nhonour....\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThat means that you will go? Very good. Certainly.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBravo!\xe2\x80\x9d--exclaimed Ip\xc3\xa1toff.--\xe2\x80\x9cWell, Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch, you have put\r\nus under an obligation. Gavr\xc3\xadlo Step\xc3\xa1nitch will simply go into\r\nraptures. Isn\xe2\x80\x99t that so, Iv\xc3\xa1n \xc3\x8dlitch?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nIv\xc3\xa1n \xc3\x8dlitch would have preferred to hold his peace, according to his\r\nwont, but thought it better to utter a sound of approval.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat possessed thee,\xe2\x80\x9d--said Pi\xc3\xb3tr Alexy\xc3\xa9itch an hour later to his\r\nsister, as he sat with her in a light two-wheeled cart, which he was\r\ndriving himself,--\xe2\x80\x9cwhat possessed thee to saddle thyself with that\r\nsour-visaged fellow for the mazurka?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI have reasons of my own for that,\xe2\x80\x9d--replied Nad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat reasons?--permit me to inquire.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThat\xe2\x80\x99s my secret.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOho!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nAnd with his whip he lightly flicked the horse, which was beginning to\r\nprick up its ears, snort, and shy. It was frightened by the shadow of a\r\nhuge willow bush which fell across the road, dimly illuminated by the\r\nmoon.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAnd shalt thou dance with M\xc3\xa1sha?\xe2\x80\x9d--Nad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna, in her turn,\r\nquestioned her brother.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes,\xe2\x80\x9d he said indifferently.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes! yes!\xe2\x80\x9d--repeated Nad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna, reproachfully.--\xe2\x80\x9cYou\r\nmen,\xe2\x80\x9d--she added, after a brief pause,--\xe2\x80\x9cpositively do not deserve to be\r\nloved by nice women.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cDost think so? Well, and that sour-visaged Petersburger--does he\r\ndeserve it?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cSooner than thou.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cReally!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nAnd Pi\xc3\xb3tr Alexy\xc3\xa9itch recited, with a sigh:\r\n\r\n    \xe2\x80\x9cWhat a mission, O Creator,\r\n     To be ... the brother of a grown-up sister!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nNad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna burst out laughing.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI cause thee a great deal of trouble, there\xe2\x80\x99s no denying that. I have a\r\ncommission to thee.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cReally?--I hadn\xe2\x80\x99t the slightest suspicion of that.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99m speaking of M\xc3\xa1sha.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOn what score?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nNad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna\xe2\x80\x99s face assumed a slight expression of pain.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThou knowest thyself,\xe2\x80\x9d--she said softly.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAh, I understand!--What\xe2\x80\x99s to be done, Nad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna, ma\xe2\x80\x99am? I\r\nlove to drink with a good friend, ma\xe2\x80\x99am, sinful man that I am; I love\r\nit, ma\xe2\x80\x99am.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cStop, brother, please don\xe2\x80\x99t talk like that!... This is no jesting\r\nmatter.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cTram-tram-tam-poom!\xe2\x80\x9d--muttered Pi\xc3\xb3tr Alexy\xc3\xa9itch through his teeth.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIt is thy perdition, and thou jestest....\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n    \xe2\x80\x9cThe farm-hand is sowing the grain, his wife does not agree....\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nstruck up Pi\xc3\xb3tr Alexy\xc3\xa9itch loudly, slapped the horse with the reins, and\r\nit dashed onward at a brisk trot.\r\n\r\n\r\nIV\r\n\r\nOn reaching home V\xc3\xa9retyeff did not undress, and a couple of hours later,\r\nwhen the flush of dawn was just colouring the sky, he was no longer in\r\nthe house.\r\n\r\nHalf-way between his estate and Ip\xc3\xa1toff\xe2\x80\x99s, on the very brink of a broad\r\nravine, stood a small birch grove. The young trees grew very close\r\ntogether, and no axe had yet touched their graceful trunks; a shadow\r\nwhich was not dense, but continuous, spread from the tiny leaves on the\r\nsoft, thin grass, all mottled with the golden heads of buttercups,[23]\r\nthe white dots of wood-campanula, and the tiny deep-crimson crosses of\r\nwild pinks. The recently-risen sun flooded the whole grove with a\r\npowerful though not brilliant light; dewdrops glittered everywhere,\r\nwhile here and there large drops kindled and glowed red; everything\r\nexhaled freshness, life, and that innocent triumph of the first moments\r\nof the morning, when everything is still so bright and still so silent.\r\nThe only thing audible was the carolling voices of the larks above the\r\ndistant fields, and in the grove itself two or three small birds were\r\nexecuting, in a leisurely manner, their brief songs, and then,\r\napparently, listening to see how their performance had turned out. From\r\nthe damp earth arose a strong, healthy scent; a pure, light breeze\r\nfluttered all about in cool gusts. Morning, glorious morning, breathed\r\nforth from everything--everything looked and smiled of the morning, like\r\nthe rosy, freshly-washed face of a baby who has just waked up.\r\n\r\nNot far from the ravine, in the middle of a small glade, on an outspread\r\ncloak, sat V\xc3\xa9retyeff. M\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna was standing beside him, leaning\r\nagainst a birch-tree, with her hands clasped behind her.\r\n\r\nBoth were silent. M\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna was gazing fixedly into the far\r\ndistance; a white scarf had slipped from her head to her shoulders, the\r\nerrant breeze was stirring and lifting the ends of her hastily-knotted\r\nhair. V\xc3\xa9retyeff sat bent over, tapping the grass with a small branch.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWell,\xe2\x80\x9d--he began at last,--\xe2\x80\x9care you angry with me?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nM\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna made no reply.\r\n\r\nV\xc3\xa9retyeff darted a glance at her.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cM\xc3\xa1sha, are you angry?\xe2\x80\x9d--he repeated.\r\n\r\nM\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna scanned him with a swift glance from head to foot turned\r\nslightly away, and said:\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat for?\xe2\x80\x9d--asked V\xc3\xa9retyeff, and flung away his branch.\r\n\r\nAgain M\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna made no reply.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBut, as a matter of fact, you have a right to be angry with me,\xe2\x80\x9d--began\r\nV\xc3\xa9retyeff, after a brief pause.--\xe2\x80\x9cYou must regard me as a man who is not\r\nonly frivolous, but even....\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou do not understand me,\xe2\x80\x9d--interrupted M\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna.--\xe2\x80\x9cI am not in\r\nthe least angry with you on my own account.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOn whose account, then?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOn your own.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nV\xc3\xa9retyeff raised his head and laughed.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAh! I understand!\xe2\x80\x9d--he said.--\xe2\x80\x9cAgain! again the thought is beginning to\r\nagitate you: \xe2\x80\x98Why don\xe2\x80\x99t I make something of myself?\xe2\x80\x99 Do you know what,\r\nM\xc3\xa1sha, you are a wonderful being; by Heaven, you are! You worry so much\r\nabout other people and so little about yourself. There is not a bit of\r\negoism in you; really, really there isn\xe2\x80\x99t. There\xe2\x80\x99s no other girl in the\r\nworld like you. It\xe2\x80\x99s a pity about one thing: I decidedly am not worthy\r\nof your affection; I say that without jesting.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cSo much the worse for you. You feel and do nothing.\xe2\x80\x9d--Again V\xc3\xa9retyeff\r\nlaughed.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cM\xc3\xa1sha, take your hand from behind your back, and give it to me,\xe2\x80\x9d--he\r\nsaid, with insinuating affection in his voice.\r\n\r\nM\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna merely shrugged her shoulders.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cGive me your beautiful, honest hand; I want to kiss it respectfully and\r\ntenderly. Thus does a giddy-pated scholar kiss the hand of his\r\ncondescending tutor.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nAnd V\xc3\xa9retyeff reached out toward M\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cEnough of that!\xe2\x80\x9d--said she. \xe2\x80\x9cYou are always laughing and jesting, and\r\nyou will jest away your life like that.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cH\xe2\x80\x99m! jest away my life! A new expression! But I hope, M\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna,\r\nthat you used the verb \xe2\x80\x98to jest\xe2\x80\x99 in the active sense?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nM\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna contracted her brows.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cEnough of that, V\xc3\xa9retyeff,\xe2\x80\x9d--she repeated.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cTo jest away life,\xe2\x80\x9d--went on V\xc3\xa9retyeff, half rising;--\xe2\x80\x9cbut you are\r\nimagining me as worse than I am; you are wasting your life in\r\nseriousness. Do you know, M\xc3\xa1sha, you remind me of a scene from P\xc3\xbashkin\xe2\x80\x99s\r\n\xe2\x80\x98Don Juan.\xe2\x80\x99 You have not read P\xc3\xbashkin\xe2\x80\x99s \xe2\x80\x98Don Juan\xe2\x80\x99?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNo.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes, I had forgotten, you see, that you do not read verses.--In that\r\npoem guests come to a certain Laura; she drives them all away and\r\nremains alone with Carlos. The two go out on the balcony; the night is\r\nwonderful. Laura admires, and Carlos suddenly begins to demonstrate to\r\nher that she will grow old in course of time.--\xe2\x80\x98Well,\xe2\x80\x99 replies Laura,\r\n\xe2\x80\x98it may be cold and rainy in Paris now, but here, with us, \xe2\x80\x9cthe night is\r\nredolent of orange and of laurel.\xe2\x80\x9d Why make guesses at the future?\xe2\x80\x99 Look\r\naround you, M\xc3\xa1sha; is it not beautiful here? See how everything is\r\nenjoying life, how young everything is. And aren\xe2\x80\x99t we young ourselves?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nV\xc3\xa9retyeff approached M\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna; she did not move away from him, but\r\nshe did not turn her head toward him.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cSmile, M\xc3\xa1sha,\xe2\x80\x9d--he went on;--\xe2\x80\x9conly with your kind smile, not with your\r\nusual grin. I love your kind smile. Raise your proud, stern eyes.--What\r\nails you? You turn away. Stretch out your hand to me, at least.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAkh, V\xc3\xa9retyeff,\xe2\x80\x9d--began M\xc3\xa1sha;--\xe2\x80\x9cyou know that I do not understand how\r\nto express myself. You have told me about that Laura. But she was a\r\nwoman, you see.... A woman may be pardoned for not thinking of the\r\nfuture.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhen you speak, M\xc3\xa1sha,\xe2\x80\x9d--returned V\xc3\xa9retyeff,--\xe2\x80\x9cyou blush incessantly\r\nwith self-love and modesty: the blood fairly flows in a crimson flood\r\ninto your cheeks. I\xe2\x80\x99m awfully fond of that in you.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nM\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna looked V\xc3\xa9retyeff straight in the eye.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cFarewell,\xe2\x80\x9d--she said, and threw her scarf over her head.\r\n\r\nV\xc3\xa9retyeff held her back. \xe2\x80\x9cEnough, enough. Stay!\xe2\x80\x9d--he cried.--\xe2\x80\x9cCome, why\r\nare you going? Issue your commands! Do you want me to enter the service,\r\nto become an agriculturist? Do you want me to publish romances with\r\naccompaniment for the guitar; to print a collection of poems, or of\r\ndrawings; to busy myself with painting, sculpture, dancing on the rope?\r\nI\xe2\x80\x99ll do anything, anything, anything you command, if only you will be\r\nsatisfied with me! Come, really now, M\xc3\xa1sha, believe me.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nAgain M\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna looked at him.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou will do all that in words only, not in deeds. You declare that you\r\nwill obey me....\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cOf course I do.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou obey, but how many times have I begged you....\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat about?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nM\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna hesitated.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNot to drink liquor,\xe2\x80\x9d--she said at last.\r\n\r\nV\xc3\xa9retyeff laughed.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cEkh, M\xc3\xa1sha! And you are at it, too! My sister is worrying herself to\r\ndeath over that also. But, in the first place, I\xe2\x80\x99m not a drunkard at\r\nall; and in the second place, do you know why I drink? Look yonder, at\r\nthat swallow.... Do you see how boldly it manages its tiny body,--and\r\nhurls it wherever it wishes? Now it has soared aloft, now it has darted\r\ndownward. It has even piped with joy: do you hear? So that\xe2\x80\x99s why I\r\ndrink, M\xc3\xa1sha, in order to feel those same sensations which that swallow\r\nexperiences.... Hurl yourself whithersoever you will, soar wheresoever\r\nyou take a fancy....\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBut to what end?\xe2\x80\x9d--interrupted M\xc3\xa1sha.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat do you mean by that? What is one to live on then?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBut isn\xe2\x80\x99t it possible to get along without liquor?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNo, it is not; we are all damaged, rumpled. There\xe2\x80\x99s passion ... it\r\nproduces the same effect. That\xe2\x80\x99s why I love you.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cLike wine.... I\xe2\x80\x99m much obliged to you.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNo, M\xc3\xa1sha, I do not love you like wine. Stay, I\xe2\x80\x99ll prove it to you\r\nsometime,--when we are married, say, and go abroad together. Do you\r\nknow, I am planning in advance how I shall lead you in front of the\r\nVenus of Milo. At this point it will be appropriate to say:\r\n\r\n    \xe2\x80\x9cAnd when she stands with serious eyes\r\n     Before the Chyprian of Milos--\r\n     Twain are they, and the marble in comparison\r\n     Suffers, it would seem, affront....\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat makes me talk constantly in poetry to-day? It must be that this\r\nmorning is affecting me. What air! \xe2\x80\x99Tis exactly as though one were\r\nquaffing wine.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWine again,\xe2\x80\x9d--remarked M\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat of that! A morning like this, and you with me, and not feel\r\nintoxicated! \xe2\x80\x98With serious eyes....\xe2\x80\x99 Yes,\xe2\x80\x9d--pursued V\xc3\xa9retyeff, gazing\r\nintently at M\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna,--\xe2\x80\x9cthat is so.... For I remember, I have\r\nbeheld, rarely, but yet I have beheld these dark, magnificent eyes, I\r\nhave beheld them tender! And how beautiful they are then! Come, don\xe2\x80\x99t\r\nturn away, M\xc3\xa1sha; pray, smile at least ... show me your eyes merry, at\r\nall events, if they will not vouchsafe me a tender glance.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cStop, V\xc3\xa9retyeff,\xe2\x80\x9d--said M\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna.--\xe2\x80\x9cRelease me! It is time for me\r\nto go home.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBut I\xe2\x80\x99m going to make you laugh,\xe2\x80\x9d--interposed V\xc3\xa9retyeff; \xe2\x80\x9cby Heaven, I\r\nwill make you laugh. Eh, by the way, yonder runs a hare....\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhere?\xe2\x80\x9d--asked M\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYonder, beyond the ravine, across the field of oats. Some one must have\r\nstartled it; they don\xe2\x80\x99t run in the morning. I\xe2\x80\x99ll stop it on the instant,\r\nif you like.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nAnd V\xc3\xa9retyeff whistled loudly. The hare immediately squatted, twitched\r\nits ears, drew up its fore paws, straightened itself up, munched,\r\nsniffed the air, and again began to munch with its lips. V\xc3\xa9retyeff\r\npromptly squatted down on his heels, like the hare, and began to twitch\r\nhis nose, sniff, and munch like it. The hare passed its paws twice\r\nacross its muzzle and shook itself,--they must have been wet with\r\ndew,--stiffened its ears, and bounded onward. V\xc3\xa9retyeff rubbed his hands\r\nover his cheeks and shook himself also.... M\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna could not\r\nhold out, and burst into a laugh.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBravo!\xe2\x80\x9d--cried V\xc3\xa9retyeff, springing up. \xe2\x80\x9cBravo! That\xe2\x80\x99s exactly the\r\npoint--you are not a coquette. Do you know, if any fashionable young\r\nlady had such teeth as you have she would laugh incessantly. But that\xe2\x80\x99s\r\nprecisely why I love you, M\xc3\xa1sha, because you are not a fashionable young\r\nlady, don\xe2\x80\x99t laugh without cause, and don\xe2\x80\x99t wear gloves on your hands,\r\nwhich it is a joy to kiss, because they are sunburned, and one feels\r\ntheir strength.... I love you, because you don\xe2\x80\x99t argue, because you are\r\nproud, taciturn, don\xe2\x80\x99t read books, don\xe2\x80\x99t love poetry....\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99ll recite some verses to you, shall I?\xe2\x80\x9d--M\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna interrupted\r\nhim, with a certain peculiar expression on her face.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cVerses?\xe2\x80\x9d--inquired V\xc3\xa9retyeff, in amazement.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes, verses; the very ones which that Petersburg gentleman recited last\r\nnight.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9c\xe2\x80\x98The Upas-Tree\xe2\x80\x99 again?... So you really were declaiming in the garden,\r\nby night? That\xe2\x80\x99s just like you.... But does it really please you so\r\nmuch?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes, it does.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cRecite it.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nM\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna was seized with shyness....\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cRecite it, recite it,\xe2\x80\x9d--repeated V\xc3\xa9retyeff.\r\n\r\nM\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna began to recite; V\xc3\xa9retyeff stood in front of her, with\r\nhis arms folded on his breast, and bent himself to listen. At the first\r\nline M\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna raised her eyes heavenward; she did not wish to\r\nencounter V\xc3\xa9retyeff\xe2\x80\x99s gaze. She recited in her even, soft voice, which\r\nreminded one of the sound of a violoncello; but when she reached the\r\nlines:\r\n\r\n    \xe2\x80\x9cAnd the poor slave expired at the feet\r\n     Of his invincible sovereign....\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nher voice began to quiver, her impassive, haughty brows rose\r\ningenuously, like those of a little girl, and her eyes, with involuntary\r\ndevotion, fixed themselves on V\xc3\xa9retyeff....\r\n\r\nHe suddenly threw himself at her feet and embraced her knees.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI am thy slave!\xe2\x80\x9d--he cried.--\xe2\x80\x9cI am at thy feet, thou art my sovereign,\r\nmy goddess, my ox-eyed Hera, my Medea....\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nM\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna attempted to repulse him, but her hands sank helplessly\r\nin his thick curls, and, with a smile of confusion, she dropped her head\r\non her breast....\r\n\r\n\r\nV\r\n\r\nGavr\xc3\xadla Step\xc3\xa1nitch Ak\xc3\xadlin, at whose house the ball was appointed,\r\nbelonged to the category of landed proprietors who evoked the\r\nadmiration of the neighbours by their ingenuity in living well on very\r\ninsignificant means. Although he did not own more than four hundred\r\nserfs, he was in the habit of entertaining the whole government in a\r\nhuge stone mansion, with a tower and a flag on the tower, erected by\r\nhimself. The property had descended to him from his father, and had\r\nnever been distinguished for being well ordered; Gavr\xc3\xadla Step\xc3\xa1nitch had\r\nbeen an absentee for a long time--had been in the service in Petersburg.\r\nAt last, twenty-five years before the date of our story, he returned to\r\nhis native place, with the rank of Collegiate Assessor,[24] and, with a\r\nwife and three daughters, had simultaneously undertaken reorganisation\r\nand building operations, had gradually set up an orchestra, and had\r\nbegun to give dinners. At first everybody had prophesied for him speedy\r\nand inevitable ruin; more than once rumours had become current to the\r\neffect that Gavr\xc3\xadla Step\xc3\xa1nitch\xe2\x80\x99s estate was to be sold under the hammer;\r\nbut the years passed, dinners, balls, banquets, concerts, followed each\r\nother in their customary order, new buildings sprang out of the earth\r\nlike mushrooms, and still Gavr\xc3\xadla Step\xc3\xa1nitch\xe2\x80\x99s estate was not sold under\r\nthe hammer, and he himself continued to live as before, and had even\r\ngrown stout of late.\r\n\r\nThen the neighbours\xe2\x80\x99 gossip took another direction; they began to hint\r\nat certain vast sums which were said to be concealed; they talked of a\r\ntreasure.... \xe2\x80\x9cAnd if he were only a good farmer, ...\xe2\x80\x9d so argued the\r\nnobles among themselves; \xe2\x80\x9cbut that\xe2\x80\x99s just what he isn\xe2\x80\x99t, you know! Not\r\nat all! So it is deserving of surprise, and incomprehensible.\xe2\x80\x9d However\r\nthat may have been, every one went very gladly to Gavr\xc3\xadla Step\xc3\xa1nitch\xe2\x80\x99s\r\nhouse. He received his guests cordially, and played cards for any stake\r\nthey liked. He was a grey-haired little man, with a small, pointed head,\r\na yellow face, and yellow eyes, always carefully shaven and perfumed\r\nwith eau-de-cologne; both on ordinary days and on holidays he wore a\r\nroomy blue dress-coat, buttoned to the chin, a large stock, in which he\r\nhad a habit of hiding his chin, and he was foppishly fastidious about\r\nhis linen; he screwed up his eyes and thrust out his lips when he took\r\nsnuff, and spoke very politely and softly, incessantly employing the\r\nletter _s_.[25]\r\n\r\nIn appearance, Gavr\xc3\xadla Step\xc3\xa1nitch was not distinguished by vivacity,\r\nand, in general, his exterior was not prepossessing, and he did not look\r\nlike a clever man, although, at times, craft gleamed in his eye. He had\r\nsettled his two elder daughters advantageously; the youngest was still\r\nat home, and of marriageable age. Gavr\xc3\xadla Step\xc3\xa1nitch also had a wife, an\r\ninsignificant and wordless being.\r\n\r\nAt seven o\xe2\x80\x99clock in the evening, Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch presented himself\r\nat the Ip\xc3\xa1toffs\xe2\x80\x99 in dress-suit and white gloves. He found them all\r\nentirely dressed; the little girls were sitting sedately, afraid of\r\nmussing their starched white frocks; old Ip\xc3\xa1toff, on catching sight of\r\nVlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch in his dress-suit, affectionately upbraided him, and\r\npointed to his own frock-coat; M\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna wore a muslin gown of a\r\ndeep rose colour, which was extremely becoming to her. Vlad\xc3\xadmir\r\nSergy\xc3\xa9itch paid her several compliments. M\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna\xe2\x80\x99s beauty\r\nattracted him, although she was evidently shy of him; he also liked\r\nNad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna, but her free-and-easy manners somewhat disconcerted\r\nhim. Moreover, in her remarks, her looks, her very smiles, mockery\r\nfrequently peeped forth, and this disturbed his citified and well-bred\r\nsoul. He would not have been averse to making fun of others with her,\r\nbut it was unpleasant to him to think that she was probably capable of\r\njeering at himself.\r\n\r\nThe ball had already begun; a good many guests had assembled, and the\r\nhome-bred orchestra was crashing and booming and screeching in the\r\ngallery, when the Ip\xc3\xa1toff family, accompanied by Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch,\r\nentered the hall of the Ak\xc3\xadlin house. The host met them at the very\r\ndoor, thanked Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch for his tender procuration of an\r\nagreeable surprise,--that was the way he expressed himself,--and, taking\r\nIp\xc3\xa1toff\xe2\x80\x99s arm, he led him to the drawing-room, to the card-tables.\r\nGavr\xc3\xadla Step\xc3\xa1nitch had received a bad education, and everything in his\r\nhouse, both the music and the furniture and the food and the wines, not\r\nonly could not be called first-class, but were not even fit to be ranked\r\nas second-class. On the other hand, there was plenty of everything, and\r\nhe himself did not put on airs, was not arrogant ... the nobles demanded\r\nnothing more from him, and were entirely satisfied with his\r\nentertainment. At supper, for instance, the caviare was served cut up in\r\nchunks and heavily salted; but no one objected to your taking it in your\r\nfingers, and there was plenty wherewith to wash it down: wines which\r\nwere cheap, it is true, but were made from grapes, nevertheless, and not\r\nsome other concoction. The springs in Gavr\xc3\xadla Step\xc3\xa1nitch\xe2\x80\x99s furniture\r\nwere rather uncomfortable, owing to their stiffness and inflexibility;\r\nbut, not to mention the fact that there were no springs whatever in many\r\nof the couches and easy-chairs, any one could place under him a worsted\r\ncushion, and there was a great number of such cushions lying about,\r\nembroidered by the hands of Gavr\xc3\xadla Step\xc3\xa1nitch\xe2\x80\x99s spouse herself--and\r\nthen there was nothing left to desire.\r\n\r\nIn a word, Gavr\xc3\xadla Step\xc3\xa1nitch\xe2\x80\x99s house could not possibly have been\r\nbetter adapted to the sociable and unceremonious style of ideas of the\r\ninhabitants of *** county, and it was solely owing to Mr. Ak\xc3\xadlin\xe2\x80\x99s\r\nmodesty that at the assemblies of the nobility he was not elected\r\nMarshal, but a retired Major Podp\xc3\xa9kin, a greatly respected and worthy\r\nman, despite the fact that he brushed his hair over to the right temple\r\nfrom the left ear, dyed his moustache a lilac hue, and as he suffered\r\nfrom asthma, had of late fallen into melancholy.\r\n\r\nSo, then, the ball had already begun. They were dancing a quadrille of\r\nten pairs. The cavaliers were the officers of a regiment stationed close\r\nby, and divers not very youthful squires, and two or three officials\r\nfrom the town. Everything was as it should be, everything was proceeding\r\nin due order. The Marshal of the Nobility was playing cards with a\r\nretired Actual Councillor of State,[26] and a wealthy gentleman, the\r\nowner of three thousand souls. The actual state councillor wore on his\r\nforefinger a ring with a diamond, talked very softly, kept the heels of\r\nhis boots closely united, and did not move them from the position used\r\nby dancers of former days, and did not turn his head, which was half\r\nconcealed by a capital velvet collar. The wealthy gentleman, on the\r\ncontrary, was constantly laughing at something or other, elevating his\r\neyebrows, and flashing the whites of his eyes. The poet Bodryak\xc3\xb3ff, a\r\nman of shy and clumsy aspect, was chatting in a corner with the learned\r\nhistorian Evsiuk\xc3\xb3ff: each had clutched the other by the button. Beside\r\nthem, one noble, with a remarkably long waist, was expounding certain\r\naudacious opinions to another noble who was timidly staring at his\r\nforehead. Along the wall sat the mammas in gay-hued caps; around the\r\ndoors pressed the men of simple cut, young fellows with perturbed faces,\r\nand elderly fellows with peaceable ones; but one cannot describe\r\neverything. We repeat: everything was as it should be.\r\n\r\nNad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna had arrived even earlier than the Ip\xc3\xa1toffs; Vlad\xc3\xadmir\r\nSergy\xc3\xa9itch saw her dancing with a young man of handsome appearance in a\r\ndandified dress-suit, with expressive eyes, thin black moustache, and\r\ngleaming teeth; a gold chain hung in a semicircle on his stomach.\r\nNad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna wore a light-blue gown with white flowers; a small\r\ngarland of the same flowers encircled her curly head; she was smiling,\r\nfluttering her fan, and gaily gazing about her; she felt that she was\r\nthe queen of the ball. Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch approached her, made his\r\nobeisance, and looking her pleasantly in the face, he asked her whether\r\nshe remembered her promise of the day before.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat promise?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhy, that you would dance the mazurka with me.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes, of course I will dance it with you.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nThe young man who stood alongside Nad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna suddenly flushed\r\ncrimson.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou have probably forgotten, mademoiselle,\xe2\x80\x9d--he began,--\xe2\x80\x9cthat you had\r\nalready previously promised to-day\xe2\x80\x99s mazurka to me.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nNad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna became confused.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAkh! good heavens, what am I to do?\xe2\x80\x9d--she said:--\xe2\x80\x9cexcuse me, pray,\r\nM\xe2\x80\x99sieu Steltch\xc3\xadnsky, I am so absent-minded; I really am ashamed....\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nM\xe2\x80\x99sieu Steltch\xc3\xadnsky made no reply, and merely dropped his eyes; Vlad\xc3\xadmir\r\nSergy\xc3\xa9itch assumed a slight air of dignity.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBe so good, M\xe2\x80\x99sieu Steltch\xc3\xadnsky,\xe2\x80\x9d--went on Nad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna; \xe2\x80\x9cyou\r\nand I are old acquaintances, but M\xe2\x80\x99sieu Ast\xc3\xa1khoff is a stranger among\r\nus; do not place me in an awkward position: permit me to dance with\r\nhim.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAs you please,\xe2\x80\x9d--returned the young man.--\xe2\x80\x9cBut you must begin.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThanks,\xe2\x80\x9d--said Nad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna, and fluttered off to meet her\r\nvis-\xc3\xa0-vis.\r\n\r\nSteltch\xc3\xadnsky followed her with his eyes, then looked at Vlad\xc3\xadmir\r\nSergy\xc3\xa9itch. Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch, in his turn, looked at him, then\r\nstepped aside.\r\n\r\nThe quadrille soon came to an end. Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch strolled about\r\nthe hall a little, then he betook himself to the drawing-room and\r\npaused at one of the card-tables. Suddenly he felt some one touch his\r\nhand from behind; he turned round--before him stood Steltch\xc3\xadnsky.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI must have a couple of words with you in the next room, if you will\r\npermit,\xe2\x80\x9d--said the latter, in French, very courteously, and with an\r\naccent which was not Russian.\r\n\r\nVlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch followed him.\r\n\r\nSteltch\xc3\xadnsky halted at a window.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIn the presence of ladies,\xe2\x80\x9d--he began, in the same language as\r\nbefore,--\xe2\x80\x9cI could not say anything else than what I did say; but I hope\r\nyou do not think that I really intend to surrender to you my right to\r\nthe mazurka with M-lle V\xc3\xa9retyeff.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nVlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch was astounded.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhy so?\xe2\x80\x9d--he asked.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBecause, sir,\xe2\x80\x9d--replied Steltch\xc3\xadnsky, quietly, laying his hand on his\r\nbreast and inflating his nostrils,--\xe2\x80\x9cI don\xe2\x80\x99t intend to,--that\xe2\x80\x99s all.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nVlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch also laid his hand on his breast, but did not\r\ninflate his nostrils.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cPermit me to remark to you, my dear sir,\xe2\x80\x9d--he began,--\xe2\x80\x9cthat by this\r\ncourse you may drag M-lle V\xc3\xa9retyeff into unpleasantness, and I\r\nassume....\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThat would be extremely unpleasant to me, but no one can prevent your\r\ndeclining, declaring that you are ill, or going away....\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI shall not do it. For whom do you take me?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIn that case, I shall be compelled to demand satisfaction from you.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cIn what sense do you mean ... satisfaction?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cThe sense is evident.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou will challenge me to a duel?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cPrecisely so, sir, if you do not renounce the mazurka.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nSteltch\xc3\xadnsky endeavoured to utter these words as negligently as\r\npossible. Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch\xe2\x80\x99s heart set to beating violently. He\r\nlooked his wholly unexpected antagonist in the face. \xe2\x80\x9cPhew, O Lord, what\r\nstupidity!\xe2\x80\x9d he thought.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYou are not jesting?\xe2\x80\x9d--he articulated aloud.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI am not in the habit of jesting in general,\xe2\x80\x9d--replied Steltch\xc3\xadnsky,\r\npompously;--\xe2\x80\x9cand particularly with people whom I do not know. You will\r\nnot renounce the mazurka?\xe2\x80\x9d--he added, after a brief pause.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI will not,\xe2\x80\x9d--retorted Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch, as though deliberating.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cVery good! We will fight to-morrow.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cVery well.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cTo-morrow morning my second will call upon you.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nAnd with a courteous inclination, Steltch\xc3\xadnsky withdrew, evidently well\r\npleased with himself.\r\n\r\nVlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch remained a few minutes longer by the window.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cJust look at that, now!\xe2\x80\x9d--he thought.--\xe2\x80\x9cThis is the result of thy new\r\nacquaintances! What possessed me to come? Good! Splendid!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nBut at last he recovered himself, and went out into the hall.\r\n\r\nIn the hall they were already dancing the polka. Before Vlad\xc3\xadmir\r\nSergy\xc3\xa9itch\xe2\x80\x99s eyes M\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna flitted past with Pi\xc3\xb3tr Alexy\xc3\xa9itch,\r\nwhom he had not noticed up to that moment; she seemed pale, and even\r\nsad; then Nad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna darted past, all beaming and joyous, with\r\nsome youthful, bow-legged, but fiery artillery officer; on the second\r\nround, she was dancing with Steltch\xc3\xadnsky. Steltch\xc3\xadnsky shook his hair\r\nviolently when he danced.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWell, my dear fellow,\xe2\x80\x9d--suddenly rang out Ip\xc3\xa1toff\xe2\x80\x99s voice behind\r\nVlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch\xe2\x80\x99s back;--\xe2\x80\x9cyou\xe2\x80\x99re only looking on, but not dancing\r\nyourself? Come, confess that, in spite of the fact that we live in a\r\ndead-calm region, so to speak, we aren\xe2\x80\x99t badly off, are we, hey?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cGood! damn the dead-calm region!\xe2\x80\x9d thought Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch, and\r\nmumbling something in reply to Ip\xc3\xa1toff, he went off to another corner of\r\nthe hall.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI must hunt up a second,\xe2\x80\x9d--he pursued his meditations;--\xe2\x80\x9cbut where the\r\ndevil am I to find one? I can\xe2\x80\x99t take V\xc3\xa9retyeff; I know no others; the\r\ndevil only knows what a stupid affair this is!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nVlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch, when he got angry, was fond of mentioning the\r\ndevil.\r\n\r\nAt this moment, Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch\xe2\x80\x99s eyes fell upon The Folding Soul,\r\nIv\xc3\xa1n \xc3\x8dlitch, standing idly by the window.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWouldn\xe2\x80\x99t he do?\xe2\x80\x9d--he thought, and shrugging his shoulders, he added\r\nalmost aloud:--\xe2\x80\x9cI shall have to take him.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nVlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch stepped up to him.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cA very strange thing has just happened to me,\xe2\x80\x9d--began our hero with a\r\nforced smile:--\xe2\x80\x9cjust imagine some young man or other, a stranger to me,\r\nhas challenged me to a duel; it is utterly impossible for me to refuse;\r\nI am in indispensable need of a second: will not you act?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nAlthough Iv\xc3\xa1n \xc3\x8dlitch was characterised, as we know, by imperturbable\r\nindifference, yet such an unexpected proposition startled even him.\r\nThoroughly perplexed, he riveted his eyes on Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cYes,\xe2\x80\x9d--repeated Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch;--\xe2\x80\x9cI should be greatly indebted to\r\nyou. I am not acquainted with any one here. You alone....\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI can\xe2\x80\x99t,\xe2\x80\x9d--said Iv\xc3\xa1n \xc3\x8dlitch, as though just waking up;--\xe2\x80\x9cI absolutely\r\ncan\xe2\x80\x99t.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhy not? You are afraid of unpleasantness; but all this will, I hope,\r\nremain a secret....\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nAs he spoke these words, Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch felt himself blushing and\r\ngrowing confused.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cExcuse me, I can\xe2\x80\x99t possibly,\xe2\x80\x9d--repeated Iv\xc3\xa1n \xc3\x8dlitch, shaking his head\r\nand drawing back, in which operation he again overturned a chair.\r\n\r\nFor the first time in his life it was his lot to reply to a request by a\r\nrefusal; but then, the request was such a queer one!\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAt any rate,\xe2\x80\x9d--pursued Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch, in an agitated voice, as he\r\ngrasped his hand,--\xe2\x80\x9cdo me the favour not to speak to any one concerning\r\nwhat I have said to you. I earnestly entreat this of you.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI can do that, I can do that,\xe2\x80\x9d--hastily replied Iv\xc3\xa1n \xc3\x8dlitch;--\xe2\x80\x9cbut the\r\nother thing I cannot do, say what you will; I positively am unable to do\r\nit.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWell, very good, very good,\xe2\x80\x9d--said Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch;--\xe2\x80\x9cbut do not\r\nforget that I rely on your discretion.... I shall announce to-morrow to\r\nthat gentleman,\xe2\x80\x9d he muttered to himself with vexation,--\xe2\x80\x9cthat I could\r\nnot find a second, so let him make what arrangements he sees fit, for I\r\nam a stranger here. And the devil prompted me to apply to that\r\ngentleman! But what else was there for me to do?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nVlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch was very, very unlike his usual self.\r\n\r\nIn the meantime, the ball went on. Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch would have\r\ngreatly liked to depart at once, but departure was not to be thought of\r\nuntil the end of the mazurka. How was he to give up to his delighted\r\nantagonist? Unhappily for Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch, the dances were in charge\r\nof a free-and-easy young gentleman with long hair and a sunken chest,\r\nover which, in semblance of a miniature waterfall, meandered a black\r\nsatin neckcloth, transfixed with a huge gold pin. This young gentleman\r\nhad the reputation, throughout the entire government, of being a man who\r\nhad assimilated, in their most delicate details, all the customs and\r\nrules of the highest society, although he had lived in Petersburg only\r\nsix months altogether, and had not succeeded in penetrating any loftier\r\nheights than the houses of Collegiate Assessor Sandar\xc3\xa1ki and his\r\nbrother-in-law, State Councillor Kostandar\xc3\xa1ki. He superintended the\r\ndances at all balls, gave the signal to the musicians by clapping his\r\nhands, and in the midst of the roar of the trumpets and the squeaking of\r\nthe violins shouted: \xe2\x80\x9c_En avant deux!_\xe2\x80\x9d or \xe2\x80\x9c_Grande cha\xc3\xaene!_\xe2\x80\x9d or \xe2\x80\x9c_A\r\nvous, mademoiselle!_\xe2\x80\x9d and was incessantly flying, all pale and\r\nperspiring, through the hall, slipping headlong, and bowing and\r\nscraping. He never began the mazurka before midnight. \xe2\x80\x9cAnd that is a\r\nconcession,\xe2\x80\x9d--he was wont to say;--\xe2\x80\x9cin Petersburg I would keep you in\r\ntorment until two o\xe2\x80\x99clock.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nThis ball seemed very long to Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch. He prowled about\r\nlike a shadow from hall to drawing-room, now and again exchanging cold\r\nglances with his antagonist, who never missed a single dance, and\r\nundertook to invite M\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna for a quadrille, but she was already\r\nengaged--and a couple of times he bandied words with the anxious host,\r\nwho appeared to be harassed by the tedium which was written on the\r\ncountenance of the new guest. At last, the music of the longed-for\r\nmazurka thundered out. Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch hunted up his lady, brought\r\ntwo chairs, and seated himself with her, near the end of the circle,\r\nalmost opposite Steltch\xc3\xadnsky.\r\n\r\nThe young man who managed affairs was in the first pair, as might have\r\nbeen expected. With what a face he began the mazurka, how he dragged his\r\nlady after him, how he beat the floor with his foot, and twitched his\r\nhead the while,--all this is almost beyond the power of human pen to\r\ndescribe.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBut it seems to me, M\xe2\x80\x99sieu Ast\xc3\xa1khoff, that you are bored,\xe2\x80\x9d--began\r\nNad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna, suddenly turning to Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI? Not in the least. What makes you think so?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhy, because I do from the expression of your face.... You have never\r\nsmiled a single time since you arrived. I had not expected that of you.\r\nIt is not becoming to you positive gentlemen to be misanthropical and\r\nto frown \xc3\xa0 la Byron. Leave that to the authors.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI notice, Nad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna, that you frequently call me a positive\r\nman, as though mockingly. It must be that you regard me as the coldest\r\nand most sensible of beings, incapable of anything which.... But do you\r\nknow, I will tell you something; a positive man is often very sad at\r\nheart, but he does not consider it necessary to display to others what\r\nis going on there inside of him; he prefers to hold his peace.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhat do you mean by that?\xe2\x80\x9d--inquired Nad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna, surveying him\r\nwith a glance.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNothing, ma\xe2\x80\x99am,\xe2\x80\x9d--replied Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch, with feigned\r\nindifference, assuming an air of mystery.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cReally?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cReally, nothing.... You shall know some day, later on.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nNad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna wanted to pursue her questions, but at that moment a\r\nyoung girl, the host\xe2\x80\x99s daughter, led up to her Steltch\xc3\xadnsky and another\r\ncavalier in blue spectacles.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cLife or death?\xe2\x80\x9d--she asked in French.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cLife,\xe2\x80\x9d--exclaimed Nad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna; \xe2\x80\x9cI don\xe2\x80\x99t want death just yet.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nSteltch\xc3\xadnsky bowed; she went off with him.[27]\r\n\r\nThe cavalier in the blue glasses, who was called Death, started off with\r\nthe host\xe2\x80\x99s daughter. Steltch\xc3\xadnsky had invented the two designations.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cTell me, please, who is that Mr. Steltch\xc3\xadnsky?\xe2\x80\x9d--inquired Vlad\xc3\xadmir\r\nSergy\xc3\xa9itch of Nad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna, as soon as the latter returned to her\r\nplace.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cHe is attached to the Governor\xe2\x80\x99s service, and is a very agreeable man.\r\nHe does not belong in these parts. He is somewhat of a coxcomb, but that\r\nruns in the blood of all of them. I hope you have not had any\r\nexplanations with him on account of the mazurka?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNone whatever, I assure you,\xe2\x80\x9d--replied Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch, with a\r\nlittle hesitation.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI\xe2\x80\x99m such a forgetful creature! You can\xe2\x80\x99t imagine!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI am bound to be delighted with your forgetfulness: it has afforded me\r\nthe pleasure of dancing with you to-night.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nNad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna gazed at him, with her eyes slightly narrowed.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cReally? You find it agreeable to dance with me?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nVlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch answered her with a compliment. Little by little he\r\ngot to talking freely. Nad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna was always charming, and\r\nparticularly so that evening; Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch thought her\r\nenchanting. The thought of the duel on the morrow, while it fretted his\r\nnerves, imparted brilliancy and vivacity to his remarks; under its\r\ninfluence he permitted himself slight exaggerations in the expression of\r\nhis feelings.... \xe2\x80\x9cI don\xe2\x80\x99t care!\xe2\x80\x9d he thought. Something mysterious,\r\ninvoluntarily sad, something elegantly-hopeless peeped forth in all his\r\nwords, in his suppressed sighs, in his glances which suddenly darkened.\r\nAt last, he got to chattering to such a degree that he began to discuss\r\nlove, women, his future, the manner in which he conceived of happiness,\r\nwhat he demanded of Fate.... He explained himself allegorically, by\r\nhints. On the eve of his possible death, Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch flirted\r\nwith Nad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna.\r\n\r\nShe listened to him attentively, laughed, shook her head, now disputed\r\nwith him, again pretended to be incredulous.... The conversation,\r\nfrequently interrupted by the approach of ladies and cavaliers, took a\r\nrather strange turn toward the end.... Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch had already\r\nbegun to interrogate Nad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna about herself, her character,\r\nher sympathies. At first she parried the questions with a jest, then,\r\nsuddenly, and quite unexpectedly to Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch, she asked him\r\nwhen he was going away.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cWhither?\xe2\x80\x9d--he said, in surprise.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cTo your own home.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cTo S\xc3\xa1sovo?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cNo, home, to your village, a hundred versts from here.\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nVlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch cast down his eyes.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cI should like to go as promptly as possible,\xe2\x80\x9d--he said with a\r\npreoccupied look on his face.--\xe2\x80\x9cTo-morrow, I think ... if I am alive.\r\nFor I have business on hand. But why have you suddenly taken it into\r\nyour head to ask me about that?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBecause I have!\xe2\x80\x9d--retorted Nad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBut what is the reason?\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBecause I have!\xe2\x80\x9d--she repeated.--\xe2\x80\x9cI am surprised at the curiosity of a\r\nman who is going away to-morrow, and to-day wants to find out about my\r\ncharacter....\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBut, pardon me ...\xe2\x80\x9d began Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch....\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAh, here, by the way ... read this,\xe2\x80\x9d--Nad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna interrupted\r\nhim with a laugh, as she handed him a motto-slip of paper from bonbons\r\nwhich she had just taken from a small table that stood near by, as she\r\nrose to meet M\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna, who had stopped in front of her with\r\nanother lady.\r\n\r\nM\xc3\xa1rya P\xc3\xa1vlovna was dancing with Pi\xc3\xb3tr Alexy\xc3\xa9itch. Her face was covered\r\nwith a flush, and was flaming, but not cheerful.\r\n\r\nVlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch glanced at the slip of paper; thereon, in wretched\r\nFrench letters, was printed:\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9c_Qui me n\xc3\xa9glige me perd._\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nHe raised his eyes, and encountered Steltch\xc3\xadnsky\xe2\x80\x99s gaze bent upon him.\r\nVlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch smiled constrainedly, threw his elbow over the back\r\nof the chair, and crossed his legs--as much as to say: \xe2\x80\x9cI don\xe2\x80\x99t care for\r\nthee!\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nThe fiery artillery officer brought Nad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna up to her chair\r\nwith a dash, pirouetted gently in front of her, bowed, clicked his\r\nspurs, and departed. She sat down.\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cAllow me to inquire,\xe2\x80\x9d--began Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch, with pauses between\r\nhis words,--\xe2\x80\x9cin what sense I am to understand this billet?...\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\n\xe2\x80\x9cBut what in the world does it say?\xe2\x80\x9d--said Nad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna.--\xe2\x80\x9cAh,\r\nyes! \xe2\x80\x98_Qui me n\xc3\xa9glige me perd._\xe2\x80\x99 Well! that\xe2\x80\x99s an admirable rule of life,\r\nwhich may be of service at every step. In order to make a success of\r\nanything, no matter what, one must not neglect anything whatsoever....\r\nOne must endeavour to obtain everything; perhaps one will obtain\r\nsomething. But I am ridiculous. I ... I am talking to you, a practical\r\nman, about rules of life....\xe2\x80\x9d\r\n\r\nNad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna burst into a laugh, and Vlad\xc3\xadmir Sergy\xc3\xa9itch strove,\r\nin vain, to the very end of the mazurka, to renew their previous\r\nconversation. Nad\xc3\xa9zhda Alexy\xc3\xa9evna avoided it with the perversity of a\r\ncapricious child.
